.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 recital 10 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n(22)On 22 September 1998 representatives of the Member States and the European Commission signed Protocols additional to the respective safeguards agreements between the Member States, the European Atomic Energy Community and the International Atomic Energy Agency, which, among other measures, oblige the Member States to provide information on transfers of specified equipment and non-nuclear material. \u00f0\u00a0Intra-Union transfer controls should allow the Member States and the Union to fulfil their obligations under these agreements.\u00a0\u00ef\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 recital 18 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n(23)It is desirable to achieve a uniform and consistent application of controls throughout the EU\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 in order to promote EU\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 and international security and to provide a level playing field for EU exporters. It is therefore appropriate, in accordance with the recommendations of the Thessaloniki Action Plan and the calls of the EU WMD Strategy, to broaden the scope of consultation \u00f0\u00a0and information exchange\u00a0\u00ef between \u00d6\u00a0the\u00a0\u00d5 Member States prior to granting an export authorisation\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0and the Commission, and to introduce tools to support the development of a common export control network throughout the Union, such as electronic licensing procedures, technical expert groups and the setting up of an enforcement coordination mechanism. While customs authorities share certain information with other customs authorities using risk management system in accordance with Union customs rules, it is also appropriate to ensure close cooperation between licensing and customs authorities\u00ef . Among the benefits of this approach would be, for example, an assurance that a Member State's essential security interests would not be threatened by an export from another Member State. Greater convergence of conditions implementing national controls on dual-use items not listed in this Regulation, and harmonisation of the conditions of use of the different types of authorisations that may be granted under this Regulation would bring about more uniform and consistent application of controls. Improving the definition of intangible transfers of technology, to include making available controlled technology to persons located outside the EU, would assist the effort to promote security as would further alignment of the modalities for exchanging sensitive information among Member States with those of the international export control regimes, in particular by providing for the possibility of establishing a secure electronic system for sharing information among Member States.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(24)It is appropriate to clarify that, to the extent that it concerns personal data, processing and exchange of information should comply with the applicable rules on processing and exchange of personal data in accordance with the rules laid down in Directive 95/46/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council\n19\n and Regulation (EC) No 45/2001 of the European Parliament and of the Council\n20\n.\n\n\n(25)Outreach to the private sector and transparency are essential elements for an effective export control regime. It is therefore appropriate to provide for the continued development of guidance to support the application of this Regulation and for the publication of an annual report on the implementation of controls, in line with current practice.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 recital 13\n\n\n(26)In order to ensure that this Regulation is properly applied, each Member State should take measures giving the competent authorities appropriate powers.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 recital 19\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n(27)Each Member State should determine effective, proportionate and dissuasive penalties applicable in the event of breach of the provisions of this Regulation,.\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0It is also appropriate to introduce provisions to tackle specifically instances of illicit trafficking of dual-use items in order to support effective enforcement of controls.\u00a0\u00ef\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 recital 11 (adapted)\n\n\n(28)The Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 has adopted a body of customs rules, contained in Council Regulation (EEC) No 2913/92 of 12 October 1992 establishing the Community Customs Code\n21\n\u00a0Council Regulation (EU) No 952/2013 of the European Parliament and of the Council\n22\n (hereinafter the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 Customs Code) and Commission Regulation (EEC) No 2454/93\n23\n implementing Regulation (EEC) No 2913/92\u00a0Wwhich lay\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0lays\u00a0\u00d5 down, among other things, provisions relating to the export and re-export of goods. Nothing in this Regulation constrains any powers under and pursuant to the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 Customs Code and its implementing provisions.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(29)Export controls have an impact on international security and trade with third countries and it is therefore appropriate to develop dialogue and cooperation with third countries in order to support a global level-playing field and enhance international security.\n\n\n(30)It is appropriate to clarify that this Regulation is without prejudice to the Commission Delegated Decision of 15 September 2015\n24\n supplementing Decision No 1104/2011/EU of the European Parliament and of the Council, which establishes specific rules for the control of the export of items for the Public Regulated Service (PRS) under the Galileo Programme.\n\n\n(31)This Regulation respects the fundamental rights and observes the principles recognised in particular by the Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union, notably the freedom to conduct business,\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 recital 17\n\n\nControls should also be introduced on the provision of brokering services when the broker has been informed by competent national authorities or is aware that such provision might lead to production or delivery of weapons of mass destruction in a third country.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n\n\nHAVE ADOPTED THIS REGULATION:\n\n\nCHAPTER I\n\n\nSUBJECT AND DEFINITIONS\n\n\nArticle 1\n\n\nThis Regulation sets up a Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 regime for the control of exports, transfer, brokering\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0, technical assistance,\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0and transit \u00d6\u00a0and transfer\u00a0\u00d5 of dual-use items.\n\n\nArticle 2\n\n\nFor the purposes of this Regulation:\n\n\n1.\u2018dual-use items\u2019 shall mean items, including software and technology, which can be used for both civil and military purposes, and shall include:\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0(a) items which can be used for the design, development, production or use of nuclear, chemical and biological weapons and their means of delivery, including\u00a0\u00ef all goods which can be used for both non-explosive uses and assisting in any way in the manufacture of nuclear weapons or other nuclear explosive devices;\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(b) cyber-surveillance technology which can be used for the commission of serious violations of human rights or international humanitarian law, or can pose a threat to international security or the essential security interests of the Union and its Member States. \n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n2.\u2018export\u2019 shall mean:\n\n\n(ia) an export procedure within the meaning of Article 161\u00a0269 of Regulation (EEC) No 2913/92 (the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 Customs Code);\n\n\n(iib) a re-export within the meaning of Article 182\u00a0270(1) of that\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0the Union Customs\u00a0\u00d5 Code but not including items in transit; and\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(c) outward processing procedure within the meaning of Article 259 of the Union Customs Code; and\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n(iiid) transmission of software or technology by electronic media, including by fax, telephone, electronic mail or any other electronic means to a destination outside the European Community; it includes making available in an electronic form such software and technology to legal and natural persons and partnerships outside the \u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Community.\u00a0Export also applies to oral transmission of technology when the technology is described over the telephone;\n\n\n3.\u2018exporter\u2019 shall mean any natural or legal person or partnership:\n\n\n(ia) on whose behalf an export \u00f0\u00a0or re-export\u00a0\u00ef declaration is made, that is to say the person who, at the time when the declaration is accepted, holds the contract with the consignee in the third country and has the power for determining the sending of the item out of the customs territory of the \u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Community. If no export contract has been concluded or if the holder of the contract does not act on its own behalf, the exporter shall mean the person who has the power for determining the sending of the item out of the customs territory of the \u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Community;\n\n\n(iib) which decides to transmit or make available software or technology by electronic media including by fax, telephone, electronic mail or by any other electronic means to a destination\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0legal and natural persons and partnerships\u00a0\u00ef outside the \u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Community.\n\n\nWhere the benefit of a right to dispose of the dual-use item belongs to a person \u00f0\u00a0resident or\u00a0\u00ef established outside the \u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Community pursuant to the contract on which the export is based, the exporter shall be considered to be the contracting party \u00f0\u00a0resident or\u00a0\u00ef established in the Community;\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union.\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n\n25\n'Exporter' shall also mean any natural person carrying the goods to be exported where these goods are contained in the person's personal baggage within the meaning of Article 1(19)(b) of Regulation (EU) 2015/2446 of 28 July 2015.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n4.\u2018export declaration\u2019 shall mean the act whereby a person indicates in the prescribed form and manner the wish to place\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0export\u00a0\u00d5 dual-use items \u00d6\u00a0specified in point 1\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0under an export procedure; \n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n5. \u2018re-export declaration\u2019 shall mean the act within the meaning of Article 5(13) of the Union Customs Code;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n\n\n56. \u2018brokering services\u2019 shall mean:\n\n\n(a) the negotiation or arrangement of transactions for the purchase, sale or supply of dual-use items from a third country to any other third country, or\n\n\n(b) the selling or buying of dual-use items that are located in third countries for their transfer to another third country.\n\n\nFor the purposes of this Regulation the sole provision of ancillary services is excluded from this definition. Ancillary services are transportation, financial services, insurance or re-insurance, or general advertising or promotion;\n\n\n67. \u2018broker\u2019 shall mean any natural or legal person or partnership resident or established in a Member State of the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0,\u00a0or a legal person or partnership owned or controlled by such person, or another person\u00a0\u00ef that carries out \u00d6\u00a0brokering\u00a0\u00d5 services defined under point 5 from the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 into the territory of a third country; \n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n8. 'technical assistance' shall mean any technical support related to repairs, development, manufacture, assembly, testing, maintenance, or any other technical service, and may take forms such as instruction, advice, training, transmission of working knowledge or skills or consulting services, including verbal forms of assistance;\n\n\n9. \u2018supplier of technical assistance\u2019 means any natural or legal person or partnership resident or established in a Member State of the Union,\u00a0or a legal person or partnership owned or controlled by such person, or another person which supplies technical assistance from the Union into the territory of a third country;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0710.\u2018transit\u2019 shall mean a transport of non-Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0non-Union\u00a0\u00d5 dual-use items entering and passing through the customs territory of the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 with a destination outside the \u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Community;\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0including items:\u00a0\u00ef\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(a)which are placed under the external transit procedure and only pass through the customs territory of the Union;\n\n\n(b)which are trans-shipped within, or directly re-exported from, a free zone;\n\n\n(c)which are in temporary storage and are directly re-exported from a temporary storage facility;\n\n\n(d)which were brought into the customs territory of the Union on the same vessel or aircraft that will take them out of that territory without unloading;\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009\n\n\n811.\u2018individual export authorisation\u2019 shall mean an authorisation granted to one specific exporter for one end user or consignee in a third country and covering one or more dual-use items;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n1012.\u2018global export authorisation\u2019 shall mean an authorisation granted to one specific exporter in respect of a type or category of dual-use item which may be valid for exports to one or more specified end users and/or in one or more specified third countries;\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n13. 'large project authorisation' shall mean a global export authorisation granted to one specific exporter, in respect of a type or category of dual-use item which may be valid for exports to one or more specified end users in one or more specified third countries for the duration of a specified project the realisation of which exceeds one year;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.1\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n914.\u2018uUnion general export authorisation\u2019 shall mean an export authorisation for exports to certain countries of destination available to all exporters who respect its conditions and requirements for use as listed in Sections\u00a0Annexes\u00a0IIa\u00a0A to IIf\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0J\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0of Annex II; \n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n15. \u2018Union general transfer authorisation\u2019 shall mean an authorisation granted for transfers of certain dual-use items between Member States available to all operators who respect its conditions and requirements for use as listed in Section A of Annex IV;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00e81\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.2\n\n\n1116.\u2018national general export authorisation\u2019 shall mean an export authorisation granted in accordance with Article 9(2) and defined by national legislation in conformity with Article 9\u00a010(6) and Section C of Annex IIIc;\n\n\n1217.\u2018customs territory of the European Union\u2019 shall mean the territory within the meaning of Article 3\u00a04 of the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 Customs Code;\n\n\n\n\n1318.\u2018non-Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0non-Union\u00a0\u00d5 dual-use items\u2019 shall mean items that have the status of non-Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0non-Union\u00a0\u00d5 goods within the meaning of Article 4(8)\u00a05(24) of the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 Customs Code.;\n\n\n219. An authorisation shall also be required for the export of dual-use items not listed in Annex I if the purchasing country or country of destination is subject to\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0'arms embargo' shall mean\u00a0\u00d5 an arms embargo \u00e81\u00a0imposed by a decision or a common position\u00a0\u00e7 adopted by the Council or a decision of the Organisation for Security and Cooperation in Europe (OSCE) or an arms embargo imposed by a binding resolution of the Security Council of the United Nations and if the exporter has been informed by the authorities referred to in paragraph 1 that the items in question are or may be intended, in their entirety or in part, for a military end-use.;\u00a0\n\n\n20.\u00a0For the purposes of this paragraph, \u2018military end-use\u2019 shall mean:\n\n\n(a) incorporation into military items listed in the military list of Member States;\n\n\n(b) use of production, test or analytical equipment and components therefor, for the development, production or maintenance of military items listed in the abovementioned list;\n\n\n(c) use of any unfinished products in a plant for the production of military items listed in the abovementioned list.;\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n21. 'cyber-surveillance technology' shall mean items specially designed to enable the covert intrusion into information and telecommunication systems with a view to monitoring, extracting, collecting and analysing data and/or incapacitating or damaging the targeted system. This includes items related to the following technology and equipment:\n\n\n(a) mobile telecommunication interception equipment;\n\n\n(b) intrusion software;\n\n\n(c) monitoring centers;\n\n\n(d) lawful interception systems and data retention systems;\n\n\n(e) digital forensics;\n\n\n\n22. 'internal compliance programme' shall mean effective, appropriate and proportionate means and procedures, including the development, implementation, and adherence to standardised operational compliance policies, procedures, standards of conduct, and safeguards, developed by exporters to ensure compliance with the provisions and with the terms and conditions of authorisations set out in this Regulation;\n\n\n23. \u2018terrorist act\u2019 shall mean a terrorist act within the meaning of Article 1(3) of Common Position 2001/931/CFSP.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\nCHAPTER II\n\n\n\n\nSCOPE\n\n\nArticle 3\n\n\n1. An authorisation shall be required for the export of the dual-use items listed in Annex I.\n\n\n2. Pursuant to Article 4 or Article 8, an authorisation may also be required for the export to all or certain destinations of certain dual-use items not listed in Annex I.\n\n\nArticle 4\n\n\n1. An authorisation shall be required for the export of dual-use items not listed in Annex I if the exporter has been informed by the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0of the Member State in which he is established that the items in question are or may be intended, in their entirety or in part,:\n\n\n(a) for use in connection with the development, production, handling, operation, maintenance, storage, detection, identification or dissemination of chemical, biological or nuclear weapons or other nuclear explosive devices or the development, production, maintenance or storage of missiles capable of delivering such weapons.;\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(b) for a military end-use if the purchasing country or country of destination is subject to an arms embargo;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n3.\u00a0(c)\u00a0An authorisation shall also be required for the export of dual-use items not listed in Annex I if the exporter has been informed by the authorities referred to in paragraph 1 that the items in question are or may be intended, in their entirety or in part for use as parts or components of military items listed in the national military list that have been exported from the territory of that\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0a\u00a0\u00d5 Member State without authorisation or in violation of an authorisation prescribed by national legislation of that Member State.;\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(d) for use by persons complicit in or responsible for directing or committing serious violations of human rights or international humanitarian law in situations of armed conflict or internal repression in the country of final destination, as identified by relevant public international institutions, or European or national competent authorities, and where there is evidence of the use of this or similar items for directing or implementing such serious violations by the proposed end-user;\n\n\n(e) for use in connection with acts of terrorism.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n\n\n42. If an exporter\u00f0, under his obligation to exercise due diligence,\u00ef is aware that dual-use items which he proposes to export, not listed in Annex I, are intended, in their entirety or in part, for any of the uses referred to in paragraphs 1, 2 and 3, he must notify the \u00d6\u00a0competent authority\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0authorities referred to in paragraph 1, which will decide whether or not it is expedient to make the export concerned subject to authorisation.\n\n\n5. A Member State may adopt or maintain national legislation imposing an authorisation requirement on the export of dual-use items not listed in Annex I if the exporter has grounds for suspecting that those items are or may be intended, in their entirety or in part, for any of the uses referred to in paragraph 1.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n3. Authorisations for the export of non-listed items shall be granted for specific items and end-users. The authorisations shall be granted by the competent authority of the Member State where the exporter is resident or established or, in case when the exporter is a person resident or established outside the Union, by the competent authority of the Member State where the items are located. The authorisations shall be valid throughout the Union. The authorisations shall be valid for one year, and may be renewed by the competent authority.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n64. A Member State which imposes an authorisation requirement, in application of paragraphs 1 to 5, 2\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0and 3\u00a0\u00ef on the export of a dual-use item not listed in Annex I, shall,\u00a0where appropriate,\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0immediately\u00a0\u00ef inform the other Member States and the Commission \u00f0\u00a0and provide them with the relevant information, in particular concerning the items and end-users concerned\u00a0\u00ef . The other Member States shall give all due consideration to this information and shall \u00f0\u00a0make known within 10 working days any objections they may have to the imposition of such an authorisation requirement. In exceptional cases, any Member State consulted may request an extension of the 10-day period. However, the extension may not exceed 30 working days. \u00ef\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0If no objections are received, the Member States consulted shall be considered to have no objection and shall impose authorisations requirements for all \"essentially similar transactions\".\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0They shall\u00a0\u00d5 inform their customs administration and other relevant national authorities \u00f0\u00a0about the authorisations requirements\u00a0\u00ef .\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nIf objections are received from any consulted Member State, the requirement for authorisation shall be revoked unless the Member State which imposes the authorisation requirement considers that an export might prejudice its essential security interests. In that case, that Member State may decide to maintain the authorisation requirement. This should be notified to the Commission and the other Member States without delay. \n\n\nThe Commission and the Member States will maintain an updated register of authorisation requirements in place.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n75. The provisions of Article 13\u00a015(1), (2) and (5) to (7) shall apply to cases concerning dual-use items not listed in Annex I.\n\n\n86. This Regulation is without prejudice to the right of Member States to take national measures under Article 11\u00a010 of Regulation (EU) 2015/479\u00a0(EEC) No 2603/69.\n\n\nArticle 5\n\n\n\n\n1. An authorisation shall be required for brokering services of dual-use items listed in Annex I if the broker has been informed by the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0of the Member State in which he is resident or established that the items in question are or may be intended, in their entirety or in part, for any of the uses referred to in Article 4(1). \n\n\n2. If a broker is aware that the dual-use items listed in Annex I for which he proposes brokering services are intended, in their entirety or in part, for any of the uses referred to in Article 4(1), he must notify the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5 which will decide whether or not it is expedient to make such brokering services subject to authorisation.\n\n\n2. A Member State may extend the application of paragraph 1 to non-listed dual-use items for uses referred to in Article 4(1) and to dual-use items for military end use and destinations referred to in Article 4(2).\n\n\n3. A Member State may adopt or maintain national legislation imposing an authorisation requirement on the brokering of dual-use items, if the broker has grounds for suspecting that these items are or may be intended for any of the uses referred to in Article 4(1).\n\n\n4. The provisions of Article 8(2), (3) and (4) shall apply to the national measures referred to in paragraphs 2 and 3 of this Article.\n\n\nArticle 6\n\n\n1. The transit of non-Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0non-Union\u00a0\u00d5 dual-use items listed in Annex I may be prohibited \u00f0\u00a0at any time\u00a0\u00ef by the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5 of the Member State where the transit occurs\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0the items are situated\u00a0\u00ef if the items are or may be intended, in their entirety or in part, for uses referred to in Article 4(1). When deciding on such a prohibition the Member States shall take into account their obligations and commitments they have agreed to as parties to international treaties or as members of international non-proliferation regimes.\n\n\n2. Before deciding whether or not to prohibit a transit a Member State may provide that its\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0the\u00a0\u00d5 competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5 may impose in individual cases an authorisation requirement for the specific transit of dual-use items listed in Annex I if the items are or may be intended, in their entirety or in part, for uses referred to in Article 4(1).\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nThe competent authority may impose the authorisation requirement on any of the following:\n\n\n(a)the declarant within the meaning of Article 5(15) of the Union Customs Code;\n\n\n(b)the carrier within the meaning of Article 5(40) of the Union Customs Code;\n\n\n(c)the natural person carrying the goods to be exported where these goods are contained in the person's personal baggage within the meaning of Article 1(19)(b) of Regulation (EU) 2015/2446.\n\n\nArticle 7\n\n\n1. An authorisation shall be required for the provision, directly or indirectly, of technical assistance related to dual-use items, or related to the provision, manufacture, maintenance and use of dual-use items, if the supplier of technical assistance has been informed by the competent authority that the items in question are or may be intended, in their entirety or in part, for any of the uses referred to in Article 4. \n\n\n2. If a supplier of technical assistance is aware that the dual-use items for which he proposes to supply technical assistance are intended, in their entirety or in part, for any of the uses referred to in Article 4, he must notify the competent authority which will decide whether or not it is expedient to make such technical assistance subject to authorisation.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n\n\n3. A Member State may extend the application of paragraph 1 to non-listed dual-use items for uses referred to in Article 4(1) and to dual-use items for military end use and destinations referred to in Article 4(2).\n\n\n4. The provisions of Article 8(2), (3) and (4) shall apply to the national measures referred to in paragraphs 2 and 3 of this Article.\n\n\nArticle 7\n\n\nThis Regulation does not apply to the supply of services or the transmission of technology if that supply or transmission involves cross-border movement of persons.\n\n\nArticle 8\n\n\n1. A Member State may prohibit or impose an authorisation requirement on the export of dual-use items not listed in Annex I for reasons of public security or \u00d6\u00a0for\u00a0\u00d5 human rights considerations.\n\n\n2. Member States shall notify the Commission \u00f0\u00a0and the other Member States\u00a0\u00ef of any measures adopted pursuant to paragraph 1 immediately after their adoption and indicate the precise reasons for the measures.\n\n\n3. Member States shall also immediately notify the Commission \u00f0\u00a0and the other Member States\u00a0\u00ef of any modifications to measures adopted pursuant to paragraph 1.\n\n\n4. The Commission shall publish the measures notified to it pursuant to paragraphs 2 and 3 in the C series of the Official Journal of the European Union.\n\n\nArticle 22\u00a09\n\n\n1. An authorisation shall be required for intra-Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0intra-Union\u00a0\u00d5 transfers of dual-use items listed in Section B of Annex IV. Items listed in Part 2 of Annex IV shall not be covered by a general authorisation.\n\n\n2. A Member State may impose an authorisation requirement for the transfer of other dual-use items from its territory to another Member State in cases where at the time of transfer:\n\n\n\u2013the operator \u00f0\u00a0or the Member State\u00a0\u00ef knows that the final destination of the items concerned is outside the \u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Community, \u00d6\u00a0and\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\n\u2013export of those items to that final destination is subject to an authorisation requirement pursuant to Articles 3, 4 or 8 in the Member State from which the items are to be transferred, and such export directly from its territory is not authorised by a general authorisation or a global authorisation, \u00d6\u00a0and\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\n\u2013no processing or working as defined in Article \u00d6\u00a060(2)\u00a0\u00d5\u00a024 of the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 Customs Code is to be performed on the items in the Member State to which they are to be transferred.\n\n\n3. The transfer authorisation must be applied for in the Member State from which the dual-use items are to be transferred.\n\n\n4. In cases where the subsequent export of the dual-use items has already been accepted, in the consultation procedures set out in Article 11, by the Member State from which the items are to be transferred, the transfer authorisation shall be issued to the operator immediately, unless the circumstances have substantially changed.\n\n\n53. A Member State which adopts legislation imposing such a requirement shall inform the Commission and the other Member States of the measures it has taken \u00f0\u00a0without delay\u00a0\u00ef . The Commission shall publish this information in the C series of the Official Journal of the European Union.\n\n\n64. The measures pursuant to paragraphs 1 and 2 shall not involve the application of internal frontier controls within the \u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Community, but solely controls which are performed as part of the normal control procedures applied in a non-discriminatory fashion throughout the territory of the \u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Community.\n\n\n75. Application of the measures pursuant to paragraphs 1 and 2 may in no case result in transfers from one Member State to another being subject to more restrictive conditions than those imposed for exports of the same items to third countries.\n\n\n\n\n96. A Member State may, by national legislation, require that, for any intra-Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0intra-Union\u00a0\u00d5 transfers from that Member State of items listed in Category 5, Part 2 of Section A of Annex I which are not listed in Section B of Annex IV, additional information concerning those items shall be provided to the competent authorities of that Member State.\n\n\n107. The relevant commercial documents relating to intra-Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0intra-Union\u00a0\u00d5 transfers of dual-use items listed in Annex I shall indicate clearly that those items are subject to controls if exported from the \u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Community. Relevant commercial documents include, in particular, any sales contract, order confirmation, invoice or dispatch note.\n\n\nCHAPTER III\n\n\nEXPORT AUTHORISATION AND AUTHORISATION FOR BROKERING SERVICES \u00d6\u00a0, TECHNICAL ASSISTANCE AND TRANSFER\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\nArticle 9\u00a010\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n1. The following authorisations for export are established under this Regulation:\n\n\n(a) individual export authorisation;\n\n\n(b) global export authorisation, including global export authorisation for large projects;\n\n\n(c) national general export authorisation;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.3(a) (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n1.\u00a0(d) Union General Export Authorisations for certain exports as set out in Sections\u00a0Annexes IIa\u00a0A to IIf\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0J\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0of Annex II\u00a0are established by this Regulation.\n\n\nAll the authorisations shall be valid throughout the \u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Community.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n2. The competent authority of the Member State where the exporter is resident or established shall be responsible for granting individual and global authorisations, for issuing national general export authorisations, as well as for all other decisions regarding the application of this Regulation to exporters resident or established on its territory.\n\n\nWhen the exporter is resident or established outside the territory of the Union, the competent authority of the Member State where the items are located shall be responsible for granting individual and global authorisations, as well as for all other decisions regarding the application of this Regulation.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle 14\n\n\n1. All individual and global export authorisations and authorisations for brokering services shall be issued \u00f0\u00a0, whenever possible,\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0in writing or by electronic means on forms containing at least all the elements and in the order set out in the models which appear in Section A of Annexes IIIa\u00a0and IIIb.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n3. Individual export authorisations and global export authorisations shall be valid for one year, and may be renewed by the competent authority. Global export authorisations for large projects shall be valid for a duration to be determined by the competent authority.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n2. For all other exports for which an authorisation is required under this Regulation, such authorisation shall be granted by the competent authorities of the Member State where the exporter is established. Subject to the restrictions specified in paragraph 4, this authorisation may be an individual, global or general authorisation.\n\n\n4. Exporters shall supply the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5 with all relevant information required for their applications for individual and global export authorisation so as to provide complete information to the national competent authorities in particular on the end user, the country of destination and the end use of the item exported. \n\n\nThe authorisation\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Authorisations\u00a0\u00d5 may be subject, if appropriate, to an end-use statement.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nGlobal export authorisations shall be subject to the implementation, by the exporter, of an effective internal compliance programme. The exporter shall also report to the competent authority, at least once a year, on the use of this authorisation; the report shall include at least the following information:\n\n\n(a) the description of the dual-use items, including the relevant control entry from Section A of Annex I;\n\n\n(b) the quantity and the value of the dual-use items;\n\n\n(c) the name and address of the consignee; \n\n\n(d) where known, the end-use and end-user of the dual-use items.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n2. At the request of exporters, global export authorisations that contain quantitative limitations shall be split.\n\n\n35. \u00d6\u00a0The competent authorities of the\u00a0\u00d5 Member States shall process requests for individual or global authorisations within a period of time to be determined by national law or practice. \u00f0\u00a0The competent authorities shall provide to the Commission all information on the average times for processing applications for authorisations relevant for the preparation of the annual report referred to in Article 24(2).\u00a0\u00ef\n\n\n46. National general export authorisations shall:\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.3(b)\n\n\n(a) exclude from their scope items listed in Section K of Annex IIg;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00e81\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.3(c)\n\n\n(b) be defined by national law or practice. They may be used by all exporters, established or resident in the Member State issuing these authorisations, if they meet the requirements set in this Regulation and in the complementary national legislation. They shall be issued in accordance with the indications set out in Section C of Annex IIIc. They shall be issued according to national law or practice;\n\n\nMember States shall notify the Commission immediately of any national general export authorisations issued or modified. The Commission shall publish these notifications in the C series of the Official Journal of the European Union;\n\n\n(c) not be used if the exporter has been informed by his authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0the competent authority\u00a0\u00d5 that the items in question are or may be intended, in their entirety or in part, for any of the uses referred to in paragraphs 1 and 3 of Article 4 or in paragraph 2 of Article 4 in a country subject to an arms embargo\u00a0\u00e81\u00a0imposed by a decision or a common position\u00a0\u00e7\u00a0adopted by the Council or a decision of the OSCE or an arms embargo imposed by a binding resolution of the Security Council of the United Nations, or if the exporter is aware that the items are intended for the abovementioned uses.\n\n\n5. Member States shall maintain or introduce in their respective national legislation the possibility of granting a global export authorisation.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.3(a)\n\n\n7. The competent authorities of the Member State where the exporter is established can prohibit the exporter from using these authorisations if there is reasonable suspicion about his ability to comply with such authorisation or with a provision of the export control legislation.\n\n\nThe competent authorities of the Member States shall exchange information on exporters deprived of the right to use a Union General Export Authorisation, unless they determine that the exporter will not attempt to export dual-use items through another Member State. The system referred to in Article 19(4)\u00a020(3) shall be used for this purpose.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle 10\u00a011\n\n\n1. Authorisations for brokering services \u00f0\u00a0and technical assistance\u00a0\u00ef under this Regulation shall be granted by the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5 of the Member State where the broker \u00f0\u00a0or the supplier of technical assistance\u00a0\u00ef is resident or established.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nWhere the broker or the supplier of technical assistance is not resident or established on the territory of the Union, authorisations for brokering services and technical assistance under this Regulation shall be granted, alternatively, by the competent authority of the Member State where the parent company of the broker or supplier of technical assistance is established, or from where the brokering services or technical assistance will be supplied.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n2. These\u00a0aAuthorisations \u00d6\u00a0for brokering services\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0and technical assistance\u00a0\u00ef shall be granted for a set quantity of specific items moving between two or more third countries. The location of the items in the originating third country, the end-user and its exact location must be clearly identified. The authorisations shall be valid throughout the \u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Community.\n\n\n23. Brokers \u00f0\u00a0and suppliers of technical assistance\u00a0\u00ef shall supply the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5 with all relevant information required for their application for authorisation under this Regulation for brokering services, in particular details of the location of the dual-use items in the originating third country, a clear description of the items and the quantity involved, third parties involved in the transaction, the third country of destination, the end-user in that country and its exact location.\n\n\n34. \u00d6\u00a0The competent authorities of the\u00a0\u00d5 Member States shall process requests for authorisations for brokering services \u00f0\u00a0and technical assistance\u00a0\u00ef within a period of time to be determined by national law or practice\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0and under the conditions as set out in Article 10(5)\u00a0\u00ef .\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n5. All authorisations for brokering services and technical assistance shall be issued, whenever possible, by electronic means on forms containing at least all the elements and in the order set out in the models which appear in Section B of Annex III.\n\n\nArticle 12\n\n\nA Union general transfer authorisation as set out in Section A of Annex IV is established by this Regulation for transfers between Member States of dual-use items listed in Section B of Annex IV.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00e81\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.4\n\n\n\u00e82\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.5\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle 11\u00a013\n\n\n1. If the dual-use items in respect of which an application has been made for an individual export authorisation to a destination not listed in Section A of\u00a0\u00e81\u00a0Annex IIa\u00a0\u00e7 or to any destination in the case of dual-use items listed in Section B of Annex IV are or will be located in one or more Member States other than the one where the application has been made, that fact shall be indicated in the application. The competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5 of the Member State to which the application for authorisation has been made shall immediately consult the competent authorities of the Member State or States in question and provide the relevant information. The Member State or States consulted shall make known within 10 working days any objections it or they may have to the granting of such an authorisation, which shall bind the Member State in which the application has been made.\n\n\nIf no objections are received within 10 working days, the Member State or States consulted shall be regarded as having no objection.\n\n\nIn exceptional cases, any Member State consulted may request the extension of the 10-day period. However, the extension may not exceed 30 working days.\n\n\n2. If an export might prejudice its essential security interests, a Member State may request another Member State not to grant an export authorisation or, if such authorisation has been granted, request its annulment, suspension, modification or revocation. The Member State receiving such a request shall immediately engage in consultations of a non-binding nature with the requesting Member State, to be terminated within 10 working days. In case the requested Member State decides to grant the authorisation, this should be notified to the Commission and other Member States using the electronic system mentioned in Article 13(6)\u00a020(3).\n\n\nArticle 12\u00a014\n\n\n1. In deciding whether or not to grant an individual or global export authorisation or to grant an authorisation for brokering services \u00f0\u00a0or technical assistance\u00a0\u00ef under this Regulation, \u00f0\u00a0or to prohibit a transit,\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0the competent authorities of\u00a0\u00d5 the Member States shall take into account all relevant considerations including\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0the following criteria\u00a0\u00ef :\n\n\n(a) \u00f0\u00a0Union and Member States\u2019 international obligations and commitments, in particular\u00a0\u00ef the obligations and commitments they have each accepted as members of the relevant international non-proliferation regimes and export control arrangements, or by ratification of relevant international treaties;,\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0and\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0(b) their obligations under sanctions imposed by \u00e82\u00a0a decision or a common position\u00a0\u00e7 adopted by the Council or by a decision of the OSCE or by a binding resolution of the Security Council of the United Nations;\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(b) respect for human rights in the country of final destination as well as respect by that country of international humanitarian law;\n\n\n(c) the internal situation in the country of final destination \u2013 competent authorities will not authorise exports that would provoke or prolong armed conflicts or aggravate existing tensions or conflicts in the country of final destination;\n\n\n(d) preservation of regional peace, security and stability;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n\n\n\n(ce) considerations of national foreign and security policy, including \u00f0\u00a0security of Member States and of territories whose external relations are the responsibility of a Member State, as well as that of friendly and allied countries\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0those covered by Council Common Position 2008/944/CFSP of 8 December 2008 defining common rules governing control of exports of military technology and equipment\n26\n;\n\n\n(df) considerations about intended end use and the risk of diversion \u00f0\u00a0, including existence of a risk that the dual-use items will be diverted or re-exported under undesirable conditions\u00a0\u00ef .\n\n\n2. In addition to the criteria set in paragraph 1, when assessing an application for a global export authorisation Member States shall take into consideration the application by the exporter of proportionate and adequate means and procedures to ensure compliance with the provisions and objectives of this Regulation and with the terms and conditions of the authorisation.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n2. The Commission and the Council shall make available guidance and/or recommendations to ensure common risk assessments by the competent authorities of the Member States for the implementation of those criteria.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle 13\u00a015\n\n\n1. The competent authorities of the Member States, acting in accordance with this Regulation, may refuse to grant an export authorisation and may annul, suspend, modify or revoke an export authorisation which they have already granted. Where they refuse, annul, suspend, substantially limit or revoke an export authorisation or when they have determined that the intended export is not to be authorised, they shall notify the competent authorities of the other Member States and the Commission thereof and share the relevant information with them. In case the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5 of a Member State have\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0has\u00a0\u00d5 suspended an export authorisation, the final assessment shall be communicated to the \u00d6\u00a0competent authorities of the other\u00a0\u00d5 Member States and the Commission at the end of the period of suspension.\n\n\n2. The competent authorities of Member States shall review denials of authorisations notified under paragraph 1 within three years of their notification and revoke them, amend them or renew them. The competent authorities of the Member States will notify the results of the review to the competent authorities of the other Member States and the Commission as soon as possible. Denials which are not revoked shall remain valid\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0and shall be reviewed within three years of their renewal\u00a0\u00ef .\n\n\n3. The competent authorities of the Member States shall notify the Member States and the Commission of their decisions to prohibit a transit of dual-use items listed in Annex I taken under Article 6 without delay. These notifications will contain all relevant information including the classification of the item, its technical parameters, the country of destination and the end user.\n\n\n4. Paragraphs 1 and 2 shall also apply to authorisations for brokering services \u00f0\u00a0and technical assistance\u00a0\u00ef .\n\n\n5. Before the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5 of a Member State, acting under this Regulation, grant\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0grants\u00a0\u00d5 an authorisation for export or brokering services \u00f0\u00a0or technical assistance,\u00a0\u00ef or decide\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0decides\u00a0\u00d5 on a transit,\u00a0they\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0it\u00a0\u00d5 shall examine all valid denials or decisions to prohibit a transit of dual-use items listed in Annex I taken under this Regulation to ascertain whether an authorisation or a transit has been denied by the competent authorities of another Member State or States for an essentially identical transaction (meaning an item with essentially identical parameters or technical characteristics to the same end user or consignee). It\u00a0They shall first consult the competent authorities of the Member State or States which issued such denial(s) or decisions to prohibit the transit as provided for in paragraphs 1 and 3. If following such consultation the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5 of the Member State decide\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0decides\u00a0\u00d5 to grant an authorisation or allow the transit, they\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0it\u00a0\u00d5 shall notify the competent authorities of the other Member States and the Commission, providing all relevant information to explain the decision.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.6\n\n\n6. All notifications required pursuant to this Article shall be made via secure electronic means including the system referred to in Article 19(4)\u00a020(3).\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\n\n7. All information shared in accordance with the provisions of this Article shall be in compliance with the provisions of Article 19\u00a020(3),\u00a0(4)\u00a0and (64) concerning the confidentiality of such information.\n\n\nCHAPTER IV\n\n\nUPDATING\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0AMENDMENT\u00a0\u00d5 OF LIST\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0LISTS\u00a0\u00d5 OF DUAL-USE ITEMS \u00d6\u00a0AND DESTINATIONS\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\nArticle 15\u00a016\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0599/2014 Art. 1.3\n\n\n1. The power to adopt delegated acts is conferred on the Commission subject to the conditions laid down in this Article.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n2. The Commission shall be empowered to adopt delegated acts in order to amend the lists of dual-use items set out in Annex I and Section B of Annex IV, as follows: \n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n1.\u00a0(a)\u00a0Tthe list of dual-use items set out in Section A of Annex I shall be updated\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0amended\u00a0\u00d5 in conformity with the relevant obligations and commitments, and any modification thereof, that Member States \u00f0\u00a0and the Union\u00a0\u00ef have accepted as members of the international non-proliferation regimes and export control arrangements, or by ratification of relevant international treaties. \u00d6\u00a0Where the amendment of Section A of Annex I concerns dual-use items which are also listed in Annexes II\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0and IV, Section B,\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0those Annexes shall be amended accordingly. \u00d5\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(b) The list of dual-use items set out in Section B of Annex I may be amended if this\u00a0is necessary due to risks that the export of such items may pose as regards the commission of serious violations of human rights or international humanitarian law or the essential security interests of the Union and its Member States.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n2.\u00a0(c)\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0The list of dual-use items set out in Section B of\u00a0\u00d5 Annex IV, which is a subset of Section A of Annex I, shall be updated\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0amended\u00a0\u00d5 with regard to Article 30\u00a0\u00d6\u00a036\u00a0\u00d5 of the Treaty \u00d6\u00a0on the Functioning of the European Union\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0establishing the European Community, namely the public policy and public security interests of the Member States.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0599/2014 Art. 1.2 (adapted)\n\n\n3. The Commission shall be empowered to adopt delegated acts in accordance with Article 23a concerning updating the list of dual-use items set out in Annex I. The updating of Annex I shall be performed within the scope set out in paragraph 1 of this Article. Where the updating of Annex I concerns dual-use items which are also listed in Annexes IIa to IIg or IV, those Annexes shall be amended accordingly.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0599/2014 Art. 1.1 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n3.\u00a0In order to ensure that only low-risk transactions are covered by the Union General Export Authorisations included in Annexes IIa to IIf,\u00a0tThe Commission shall be empowered to adopt delegated acts in accordance with Article 23a to \u00d6\u00a0amend Annex II\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0by adding or\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0remove\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0removing\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0items or\u00a0\u00ef destinations from the scope of those Union Ggeneral Eexport Aauthorisations \u00d6\u00a0set out in Annex II\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0in consideration of the criteria set out in Article 14\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0, if such destinations become subject to an arms embargo as referred to in Article 4(2). Where,\u00a0in cases of such arms embargoes, imperative grounds of urgency require a removal of particular destinations from the scope of a Union Ggeneral Eexport Aauthorisation, the procedure provided for in Article 23b\u00a017 shall apply to delegated acts adopted pursuant to this paragraph.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0599/2014 Art. 1.3 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle 23a\n\n\n24. The power to adopt delegated acts referred to in this Article 9(1) and Article 15(3) shall be conferred on the Commission for a period of five years from 2 July 2014\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0the entry into force of this Regulation\u00a0\u00ef . The Commission shall draw up a report in respect of the delegation of power not later than nine months before the end of the five-year period. The delegation of power shall be tacitly extended for periods of an identical duration, unless the European Parliament or the Council opposes such extension not later than three months before the end of each period.\n\n\n35. The delegation of power referred to in this Article 9(1) and Article 15(3) may be revoked at any time by the European Parliament or by the Council. A decision to revoke shall put an end to the delegation of the power specified in that decision. It shall take effect the day following the publication of the decision in the Official Journal of the European Union or at a later date specified therein. It shall not affect the validity of any delegated acts already in force.\n\n\n\u00d6\u00a06. Before adopting a delegated act, the Commission shall consult experts designated by each Member State in accordance with the principles laid down in the Inter-Institutional Agreement on Better Law-Making of 13 April 2016.\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\n47. As soon as it adopts a delegated act, the Commission shall notify it simultaneously to the European Parliament and to the Council.\n\n\n58. A delegated act adopted pursuant to this Article 9(1) and Article 15(3) shall enter into force only if no objection has been expressed either by the European Parliament or the Council within a period of two months of notification of that act to the European Parliament and the Council or if, before the expiry of that period, the European Parliament and the Council have both informed the Commission that they will not object. That period shall be extended by two months at the initiative of the European Parliament or of the Council.\n\n\nArticle 23b\u00a017\n\n\n1. Delegated acts adopted under this Article shall enter into force without delay and shall apply as long as no objection is expressed in accordance with paragraph 2. The notification of a delegated act to the European Parliament and to the Council shall state the reasons for the use of the urgency procedure.\n\n\n2. Either the European Parliament or the Council may object to a delegated act in accordance with the procedure referred to in this Article 23a(5). In such a case, the Commission shall repeal the act without delay following the notification of the decision to object by the European Parliament or by the Council.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nCHAPTER V\n\n\nCUSTOMS PROCEDURES\n\n\nArticle 16\u00a018\n\n\n1. When completing the formalities for the export of dual-use items at the customs office responsible for handling the export declaration, the exporter shall furnish proof that any necessary export authorisation has been obtained.\n\n\n2. A translation of any documents furnished as proof into an official language of the Member State where the export declaration is presented may be required of the exporter.\n\n\n3. Without prejudice to any powers conferred on it under, and pursuant to, the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 Customs Code, a Member State may also, for a period not exceeding the periods referred to in paragraph 4, suspend the process of export from its territory, or, if necessary, otherwise prevent the dual-use items listed in Annex I which are covered by a valid export authorisation from leaving the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 via its territory, where it has grounds for suspicion that:\n\n\n(a) relevant information was not taken into account when the authorisation was granted, or\n\n\n(b) circumstances have materially changed since the grant of the authorisation.\n\n\n4. In the case referred to in paragraph 3, the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5 of the Member State which granted the export authorisation shall be consulted forthwith in order that they may take action pursuant to Article 13\u00a015(1). If such competent authorities decide\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority decides\u00a0\u00d5 to maintain the authorisation, they\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0it\u00a0\u00d5 shall reply within 10 working days, which, at their\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0its\u00a0\u00d5 request, may be extended to 30 working days in exceptional circumstances. In such case, or if no reply is received within 10 or 30 days, as the case may be, the dual-use items shall be released immediately. The \u00d6\u00a0competent authority of the\u00a0\u00d5 Member State which granted the authorisation shall inform \u00d6\u00a0the competent authorities of\u00a0\u00d5 the other Member States and the Commission.\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a05. The Commission, in cooperation with the Member States, shall develop a guidance to support interagency cooperation between licensing and customs authorities.\u00a0\u00ef\n\n\nArticle 17\u00a019\n\n\n1. Member States may provide that customs formalities for the export of dual-use items may be completed only at customs offices empowered to that end.\n\n\n2. Member States availing themselves of the option set out in paragraph 1 shall inform the Commission of the duly empowered customs offices. The Commission shall publish the information in the C series of the Official Journal of the European Union.\n\n\nArticle 18\n\n\nThe provisions of Articles 843 and 912a to 912g of Regulation (EEC) No 2454/93 shall apply to the restrictions relating to the export, re-export and exit from the customs territory of dual-use items for the export of which an authorisation is required under this Regulation.\n\n\nCHAPTER VI\n\n\nADMINISTRATIVE COOPERATION \u00d6\u00a0, IMPLEMENTATION AND ENFORCEMENT\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\nArticle 19\u00a020\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.9 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n1. Each Member State\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0States\u00a0\u00d5 shall inform the Commission \u00f0\u00a0without delay\u00a0\u00ef of the laws, regulations and administrative provisions adopted in implementation of this Regulation, including:\u00a0the measures referred to in Article 24. The Commission shall forward the information to the other Member States.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n6.\u00a0(a)\u00a0Member States shall supply the Commission with a list of the authorities empowered to:\n\n\n\u2013(a) grant export authorisations for dual-use items;\n\n\n\u20134.\u00a0Member States shall supply the Commission with a list of the authorities empowered to grant authorisations under this Regulation for the provision of brokering services \u00f0\u00a0and technical assistance\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0.;\u00a0The Commission shall publish the list of these authorities in the C series of the Official Journal of the European Union.\n\n\n\u2013(b) decide to prohibit the transit of non-Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0non-Union\u00a0\u00d5 dual-use items under this Regulation.;\n\n\n\u00d6\u00a0(b) the measures referred to in Article 22.\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\nThe Commission \u00d6\u00a0shall forward the information to the other Member States and\u00a0\u00d5 shall publish the list of these authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0information\u00a0\u00d5 in the C series of the Official Journal of the European Union.\n\n\n12. Member States, in cooperation with the Commission, shall take all appropriate measures to establish direct cooperation and exchange of information between \u00d6\u00a0the\u00a0\u00d5 competent authorities,\u00a0in particular to eliminate the risk that possible disparities in the application of export controls to dual-use items may lead to a deflection of trade, which could create difficulties for one or more Member States.\n\n\n2. Member States shall take all appropriate measures to establish direct cooperation and exchange of information between competent authorities with a view to enhance the efficiency of the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 export control regime \u00f0\u00a0and to ensure the consistent and effective implementation and enforcement of control throughout the EU\u00a0\u00ef . Such information may\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0shall\u00a0\u00ef include:\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(a) information regarding the application of controls, including licensing data (number, value and types of licences and related destinations, number of users of general and global authorisations, number of operators with ICPs, processing times, volume and value of trade subject to intra-EU transfers etc), and, where available, data on exports of dual-use items carried out in other Member States;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\n\n\u00e81\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.7(a)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n(ab) \u00f0\u00a0information regarding the enforcement of controls, including\u00a0\u00ef details of exporters deprived,\u00a0by national sanctions, of the right to use the national \u00d6\u00a0or\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 general export authorisations or\u00a0\u00e81\u00a0Union General Export Authorisations\u00a0\u00e7\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0, reports of violations, seizures and the application of other penalties\u00a0\u00ef ;\n\n\n(bc) data on sensitive end users, actors involved in suspicious procurement activities, and, where available, routes taken.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009\n\n\n3. Council Regulation (EC) No 515/97 of 13 March 1997 on mutual assistance between the administrative authorities of the Member States and cooperation between the latter and the Commission to ensure the correct application of the law on customs and agricultural matters\n27\n, and in particular the provisions on the confidentiality of information, shall apply mutatis mutandis, without prejudice to Article 23 of this Regulation.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.7(b) (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n43. A secure and encrypted system for the exchange of information between Member States and, where appropriate, the Commission shall \u00f0\u00a0be developed\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0set up by the Commission, in consultation with the Dual-Use Coordination Group set up pursuant to Article 23\u00a021, \u00f0\u00a0to support direct cooperation and exchange of information between the competent authorities of the Member States and the Commission\u00ef. \u00f0\u00a0The system shall be connected, where appropriate, to the electronic licensing systems of the competent authorities of the Member States.\u00a0\u00ef The European Parliament shall be informed about the system\u2019s budget, development,\u00a0provisional and final set-up and functioning, and network costs.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n64. The processing of personal data shall be in accordance with the rules laid down in Directive 95/46/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 24 October 1995 on the protection of individuals with regard to the processing of personal data and on the free movement of such data\n28\n and Regulation (EC) No 45/2001 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 18 December 2000 on the protection of individuals with regard to the processing of personal data by the Community institutions and bodies and on the free movement of such data\n29\n. \u00f0 Personal data shall be used by the competent authorities of the Member States and the Commission only for the purpose of implementation and enforcement of this Regulation and in light of its objectives. These data shall be retained for the duration of the measures adopted by the competent authorities of the Member States pursuant to this Regulation and their renewal or amendment.\u00a0\u00ef\n\n\nArticle 23\u00a021\n\n\n1. A Dual-Use Coordination Group chaired by a representative of the Commission shall be set up. Each Member State shall appoint a representative to this Group. It shall examine any question concerning the application of this Regulation which may be raised either by the chair or by a representative of a Member State.\n\n\n2. The Chair of the Dual-Use Coordination Group or the Coordination Group shall, whenever it considers it to be necessary, consult exporters, brokers and other relevant stakeholders concerned by this Regulation.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n\n\n3. The Dual-Use Coordination Group shall, where appropriate, set up technical expert groups composed of experts from Member States to examine specific issues relating to the implementation of controls, including issues relating to the updating of the Union control lists in Annex I. Technical expert groups shall, where appropriate, consult exporters, brokers and other relevant stakeholders concerned by this Regulation.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009\n\n\nArticle 24\u00a022\n\n\n1. Each Member State shall take appropriate measures to ensure proper enforcement of all the provisions of this Regulation. In particular, it shall lay down the penalties applicable to infringements of the provisions of this Regulation or of those adopted for its implementation. Those penalties must be effective, proportionate and dissuasive.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n2. The Dual-Use Coordination Group shall set up an Enforcement Coordination Mechanism with a view to establish direct cooperation and exchange of information between competent authorities and enforcement agencies.\n\n\nArticle 23\n\n\nIt shall be prohibited to participate, knowingly and intentionally, in activities the object or effect of which is to circumvent the measures referred to in Article 3, 4, 5, 6, and 7.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nCHAPTER VII\n\n\n\u00d6\u00a0TRANSPARENCY, OUTREACH, MONITORING, EVALUATION\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\nArticle 24\n\n\n51. The provision of guidance to exporters and brokers will be the responsibility of the Member States where they are resident or established. The Commission and the Council may\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0shall, where appropriate,\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0also make available guidance and/or recommendations for best practices for the subjects referred to in this Regulation \u00f0\u00a0to ensure the efficiency of the Union export control regime and the consistency of its implementation\u00a0\u00ef . \u00f0\u00a0The competent authorities of the Member States shall also, where appropriate, provide complementary guidance for exporters, brokers and transit operators resident or established in that Member State.\u00a0\u00ef\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.8 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n\n\n32. The Commission shall submit an annual report to the European Parliament \u00f0\u00a0and the Council on the implementation and enforcement of controls in the Union and\u00a0\u00ef on the activities, examinations and consultations of the Dual-Use Coordination Group, which shall be subject to Article 4 of Regulation (EC) No 1049/2001 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 30 May 2001 regarding public access to European Parliament, Council and Commission documents\n30\n.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.9\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n2. Every 3 years the Commission shall review the implementation of this Regulation and present a comprehensive implementation and impact assessment report to the European Parliament and the Council, which may include proposals for its amendment. Member States shall provide to the Commission all appropriate information for the preparation of the report. \u00f0\u00a0This annual report shall be public.\u00a0\u00ef\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n3. Between five and seven years after the date of application of this Regulation, the Commission shall carry out an evaluation of this Regulation and report on the main findings to the European Parliament, the Council and the European Economic and Social Committee. \n\n\nMember States shall be involved in this exercise and shall provide the Commission with necessary information for the preparation of that report.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nCHAPTER VII\u00a0VIII\n\n\nCONTROL MEASURES\n\n\nArticle 20\u00a025\n\n\n1. Exporters of dual-use items shall keep detailed registers or records of their exports, in accordance with the national law or practice in force in the respective Member States. Such registers or records shall include in particular commercial documents such as invoices, manifests and transport and other dispatch documents containing sufficient information to allow the following to be identified:\n\n\n(a) the description of the dual-use items;\n\n\n(b) the quantity of the dual-use items;\n\n\n(c) the name and address of the exporter and of the consignee;\n\n\n(d) where known, the end-use and end-user of the dual-use items.\n\n\n\n\n2. In accordance with national law or practice in force in the respective Member States, brokers \u00f0\u00a0and suppliers of technical assistance\u00a0\u00ef shall keep registers or records for brokering \u00f0\u00a0or technical assistance\u00a0\u00ef services which fall under the scope of Article 5 so as to be able to prove, on request, the description of the dual-use items that were the subject of brokering \u00f0\u00a0or technical assistance\u00a0\u00ef services, the period during which the items were the subject of such services and their destination, and the countries concerned by those brokering services.\n\n\n3. The registers or records and the documents referred to in paragraphs 1 and 2 shall be kept for at least three years from the end of the calendar year in which the export took place or the brokering \u00f0\u00a0or technical assistance\u00a0\u00ef services were provided. They shall be produced, on request, to the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0of the Member State in which the exporter is established or the broker is established or resident.\n\n\n84. Documents and records of intra-Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0intra-Union\u00a0\u00d5 transfers of dual-use items listed in Annex I shall be kept for at least three years from the end of the calendar year in which a transfer took place and shall be produced to the competent authorities\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0authority\u00a0\u00d5 of the Member State from which these items were transferred on request.\n\n\nArticle 21\u00a026\n\n\nIn order to ensure that this Regulation is properly applied, each Member State shall take whatever measures are needed to permit its competent authorities:\n\n\n(a) to gather information on any order or transaction involving dual-use items;\n\n\n(b) to establish that the export control measures are being properly applied, which may include in particular the power to enter the premises of persons with an interest in an export transaction or brokers involved in the supply of brokering services under circumstances set out in Article 5 \u00f0\u00a0, or suppliers of technical assistance under the circumstances set out in Article 7\u00a0\u00ef .\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.10 (adapted)\n\n\nCHAPTER IX\n\n\n\u00d6\u00a0COOPERATION WITH THIRD COUNTRIES\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\nArticle 25a\u00a027\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n1. The Commission and the competent authorities of the Member States shall, where appropriate, maintain regular and reciprocal exchange of information with third countries.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.10\n\n\n2. Without prejudice to the provisions on mutual administrative assistance agreements or protocols in customs matters concluded between the Union and third countries, the Council may authorise the Commission to negotiate with third countries agreements providing for the mutual recognition of export controls of dual-use items covered by this Regulation and in particular:\n\n\n(a) to eliminate authorisation requirements for re-exports within the territory of the Union.;\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(b) to enable the post-shipment verification of exports in third countries;\n\n\n(c) to develop end-user verification programmes for trusted end-users in third countries.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.10\n\n\nThese negotiations shall be conducted in accordance with the procedures established in Article 207(3) of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union and the Treaty establishing the European Atomic Energy Community, as appropriate.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009\n\n\nCHAPTER VIII X\n\n\nOTHER PROVISIONS\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a01232/2011 Art. 1.9\n\n\nArticle 25\n\n\n3. Special sections of the report shall deal with:\n\n\n(a) the Dual-Use Coordination Group and its activities. Information that the Commission provides on the Dual-Use Coordination Group\u2019s examinations and consultations shall be treated as confidential pursuant to Article 4 of Regulation (EC) No 1049/2001. Information shall in any case be considered to be confidential if its disclosure is likely to have a significantly adverse effect upon the supplier or the source of such information;\n\n\n(b) the implementation of Article 19(4), and shall report on the stage reached in the set-up of the secure and encrypted system for the exchange of information between Member States and the Commission;\n\n\n(c) the implementation of Article 15(1);\n\n\n(d) the implementation of Article 15(2);\n\n\n(e) comprehensive information provided on the measures taken by the Member States pursuant to Article 24 and notified to the Commission under paragraph 1 of this Article.\n\n\n4. No later than 31 December 2013, the Commission shall submit to the European Parliament and to the Council a report evaluating the implementation of this Regulation with a specific focus on the implementation of Annex IIb, Union General Export Authorisation No EU002, accompanied by, if appropriate, a legislative proposal to amend this Regulation, in particular as regards the issue of low-value shipments.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0428/2009 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle 26\u00a028\n\n\nThis Regulation does not affect:\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0is without prejudice to the Commission Delegated Decision of 15 September 2015 supplementing Decision No 1104/2011/EU of the European Parliament and of the Council.\u00a0\u00ef\n\n\n\u2013the application of Article 296 of the Treaty establishing the European Community,\n\n\n\u2013the application of the Treaty establishing the European Atomic Energy Community.\n\n\nArticle 27\u00a029\n\n\nRegulation (EC) No 1334/2000\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0428/2009\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0is repealed with effect from 27 August 2009\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0[\u2026]\u00a0\u00d5 .\n\n\nHowever, for export authorisation applications made before 27 August 2009\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0[\u2026]\u00a0\u00d5 , the relevant provisions of Regulation (EC) No 1334/2000\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0428/2009\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0shall continue to apply.\n\n\nReferences to the repealed Regulation shall be construed as references to this Regulation and shall be read in accordance with the correlation table in Annex VI.\n\n\nArticle 28\u00a030\n\n\nThis Regulation shall enter into force 90 days after the date\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0on the ninetieth day following that\u00a0\u00d5 of its publication in the Official Journal of the European Union.\n\n\nThis Regulation shall be binding in its entirety and directly applicable in all Member States.\n\n\nDone at Brussels,\n\n\n\nFor the European Parliament\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0For the Council\n\n\nThe
