and\n\n\n4.Capable of in-situ steam sterilisation in a closed state;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nCentrifugal separators include decanters.\n\n\nd.Cross (tangential) flow filtration equipment and components as follows:\n\n\n1.Cross (tangential) flow filtration equipment capable of separation of pathogenic micro-organisms, viruses, toxins or cell cultures having all of the following characteristics:\n\n\na.A total filtration area equal to or greater than 1 m2; and\n\n\nb.Having any of the following characteristics:\n\n\n1.Capable of being sterilised or disinfected in-situ; or\n\n\n\n\n2.Using disposable or single-use filtration components;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nIn 2B352.d.1.b. sterlised denotes the elimination of all viable microbes from the equipment through the use of either physical (e.g. steam) or chemical agents. Disinfected denotes the destruction of potential microbial infectivity in the equipment through the use of chemical agents with a germicidal effect. Disinfection and sterilisation are distinct from sanitisation, the latter referring to cleaning procedures designed to lower the microbial content of equipment without necessarily achieving elimination of all microbial infectivity or viability.\n\n\nNote:2B352.d. does not control reverse osmosis equipment, as specified by the manufacturer.\n\n\n2.Cross (tangential) flow filtration components (e.g. modules, elements, cassettes, cartridges, units or plates) with filtration area equal to or greater than 0,2 m2 for each component and designed for use in cross (tangential) flow filtration equipment specified in 2B352.d.;\n\n\ne.Steam sterilisable freeze drying equipment with a condenser capacity exceeding 10 kg of ice in 24 hours and less than 1000 kg of ice in 24 hours;\n\n\nf.Protective and containment equipment, as follows:\n\n\n1.Protective full or half suits, or hoods dependent upon a tethered external air supply and operating under positive pressure;\n\n\nNote:2B352.f.1. does not control suits designed to be worn with self-contained breathing apparatus.\n\n\n2.Class III biological safety cabinets or isolators with similar performance standards;\n\n\nNote:In 2B352.f.2., isolators include flexible isolators, dry boxes, anaerobic chambers, glove boxes and laminar flow hoods (closed with vertical flow).\n\n\ng.Chambers designed for aerosol challenge testing with \"microorganisms\", viruses or \"toxins\" and having a capacity of 1 m3 or greater;\n\n\nh.Spray drying equipment capable of drying toxins or pathogenic microorganisms having all of the following:\n\n\n1.A water evaporation capacity of \u2265 0,4 kg/h and \u2264 400 kg/h;\n\n\n2.The ability to generate a typical mean product particle size of \u226410 \u03bcm with existing fittings or by minimal modification of the spray-dryer with atomization nozzles enabling generation of the required particle size; and\n\n\n3.Capable of being sterilised or disinfected in situ.\n\n\n2CMaterials\n\n\nNone.\n\n\n2DSoftware\n\n\n2D001\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Software\", other than that specified in 2D002, as follows:\n\n\n\n\na.\"Software\" specially designed or modified for the \"development\" or \"production\" of equipment specified in 2A001 or 2B001\n\n\nb.\"Software\" specially designed or modified for the \"use\" of equipment specified in 2A001.c, 2B001 or 2B003 to 2B009.\n\n\nNote:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a02D001 does not control part programming \"software\" that generates \"numerical control\" codes for machining various parts.\n\n\n2D002\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Software\" for electronic devices, even when residing in an electronic device or system, enabling such devices or systems to function as a \"numerical control\" unit, capable of co-ordinating simultaneously more than four axes for \"contouring control\".\n\n\nNote 1:2D002 does not control \"software\" specially designed or modified for the operation of items not specified in Category 2.\n\n\nNote 2:2D002 does not control \"software\" for items specified in 2B002. See 2D001 and 2D003 for \"software\" for items specified in 2B002.\n\n\nNote 3:2D002 does not control \"software\" that is exported with, and the minimum necessary for the operation of, items not specified by Category 2.\n\n\n2D003\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Software\", designed or modified for the operation of equipment specified in 2B002, that converts optical design, workpiece measurements and material removal functions into \"numerical control\" commands to achieve the desired workpiece form.\n\n\n2D101\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Software\" specially designed or modified for the \"use\" of equipment for machining various parts.\n\n\n2D351\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Software\", other than that specified in 1D003, specially designed for \"use\" of equipment specified in across from the relevant Substrate under column 2. repair and refurbishing as well as original coating.\n\n\n2.The term 'alloyed aluminide coating' includes single or multiple-step coatings in which an element or elements are deposited prior to or during application of the aluminide coating, even if these elements are deposited by another coating process. It does not, however, include the multiple use of single-step pack cementation processes to achieve alloyed aluminides.\n\n\n3.The term 'noble metal modified aluminide' coating includes multiple-step coatings in which the noble metal or noble metals are laid down by some other coating process prior to application of the aluminide coating.\n\n\n4.The term 'mixtures thereof' includes infiltrated material, graded compositions, co-deposits and multilayer deposits and are obtained by one or more of the coating processes specified in the Table.\n\n\n5.'MCrAlX' refers to a coating alloy where M equals cobalt, iron, nickel or combinations thereof and X equals hafnium, yttrium, silicon, tantalum in any amount or other intentional additions over 0,01 % by weight in various proportions and combinations, except:\n\n\na.CoCrAlY coatings which contain less than 22 % by weight of chromium, less than 7 % by weight of aluminium and less than 2 % by weight of yttrium;\n\n\n\n\nb.CoCrAlY coatings which contain 22 to 24 % by weight of chromium, 10 to 12 % by weight of aluminium and 0,5 to 0,7 % by weight of yttrium; or\n\n\nc.NiCrAlY coatings which contain 21 to 23 % by weight of chromium, 10 to 12 % by weight of aluminium and 0,9 to 1,1 % by weight of yttrium.\n\n\n6.The term 'aluminium alloys' refers to alloys having an ultimate tensile strength of 190 MPa or more measured at 293 K (20 \u00b0C).\n\n\n7.The term 'corrosion resistant steel' refers to AISI (American Iron and Steel Institute) 300 series or equivalent national standard steels.\n\n\n8.'Refractory metals and alloys' include the following metals and their alloys: niobium (columbium), molybdenum, tungsten and tantalum.\n\n\n9.'Sensor window materials', as follows: alumina, silicon, germanium, zinc sulphide, zinc selenide, gallium arsenide, diamond, gallium phosphide, sapphire and the following metal halides: sensor window materials of more than 40 mm diameter for zirconium fluoride and hafnium fluoride.\n\n\n10.\"Technology\" for single-step pack cementation of solid airfoils is not controlled by Category 2.\n\n\n11.'Polymers', as follows: polyimide, polyester, polysulphide, polycarbonates and polyurethanes.\n\n\n12.'Modified zirconia' refers to additions of other metal oxides (e.g., calcia, magnesia, yttria, hafnia, rare earth oxides) to zirconia in order to stabilise certain crystallographic phases and phase compositions. Thermal barrier coatings made of zirconia, modified with calcia or magnesia by mixing or fusion, are not controlled.\n\n\n13.'Titanium alloys' refers only to aerospace alloys having an ultimate tensile strength of 900 MPa or more measured at 293 K (20 \u00b0C).\n\n\n14.'Low-expansion glasses' refers to glasses which have a coefficient of thermal expansion of 1 \u00d7 10\u20137 K\u20131 or less measured at 293 K (20 \u00b0C).\n\n\n15.'Dielectric layers' are coatings constructed of multi-layers of insulator materials in which the interference properties of a design composed of materials of various refractive indices are used to reflect, transmit or absorb various wavelength bands. Dielectric layers refers to more than four dielectric layers or dielectric/metal \"composite\" layers.\n\n\n16.'Cemented tungsten carbide' does not include cutting and forming tool materials consisting of tungsten carbide/(cobalt, nickel), titanium carbide/(cobalt, nickel), chromium carbide/nickel-chromium and chromium carbide/nickel.\n\n\n17.\"Technology\" specially designed to deposit diamond-like carbon on any of the following is not controlled:\n\n\nmagnetic disk drives and heads, equipment for the manufacture of disposables, valves for faucets, acoustic diaphragms for speakers, engine parts for automobiles, cutting tools, punching-pressing dies, office automation equipment, microphones or medical devices or moulds, for casting or moulding of plastics, manufactured from alloys containing less than 5 % beryllium.\n\n\n18.'Silicon carbide' does not include cutting and forming tool materials.\n\n\n19.Ceramic substrates, as used in this entry, does not include ceramic materials containing 5 % by weight, or greater, clay or cement content, either as separate constituents or in combination.\n\n\nTABLE \u2014\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0DEPOSITION TECHNIQUES \u2014\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0TECHNICAL NOTE\n\n\nProcesses specified in Column 1 of the Table are defined as follows:\n\n\na.Chemical Vapour Deposition (CVD) is an overlay coating or surface modification coating process wherein a metal, alloy, \"composite\", dielectric or ceramic is deposited upon a heated substrate. Gaseous reactants are decomposed or combined in the vicinity of a substrate resulting in the deposition of the desired elemental, alloy or compound material on the substrate. Energy for this decomposition or chemical reaction process may be provided by the heat of the substrate, a glow discharge plasma, or \"laser\" irradiation.\n\n\n\n\nN.B. 1CVD includes the following processes: directed gas flow out-of-pack deposition, pulsating CVD, controlled nucleation thermal deposition (CNTD), plasma enhanced or plasma assisted CVD processes.\n\n\nN.B. 2Pack denotes a substrate immersed in a powder mixture.\n\n\nN.B. 3The gaseous reactants used in the out-of-pack process are produced using the same basic reactions and parameters as the pack cementation process, except that the substrate to be coated is not in contact with the powder mixture.\n\n\nb.Thermal Evaporation-Physical Vapour Deposition (TE-PVD) is an overlay coating process conducted in a vacuum with a pressure less than 0,1 Pa wherein a source of thermal energy is used to vaporize the coating material. This process results in the condensation, or deposition, of the evaporated species onto appropriately positioned substrates.\n\n\nThe addition of gases to the vacuum chamber during the coating process to synthesize compound coatings is an ordinary modification of the process.\n\n\nThe use of ion or electron beams, or plasma, to activate or assist the coating's deposition is also a common modification in this technique. The use of monitors to provide in-process measurement of optical characteristics and thickness of coatings can be a feature of these processes.\n\n\nSpecific TE-PVD processes are as follows:\n\n\n1.Electron Beam PVD uses an electron beam to heat and evaporate the material which forms the coating;\n\n\n2.Ion Assisted Resistive Heating PVD employs electrically resistive heating sources in combination with impinging ion beam(s) to produce a controlled and uniform flux of evaporated coating species;\n\n\n3.\"Laser\" Vaporization uses either pulsed or continuous wave \"laser\" beams to vaporize the material which forms the coating;\n\n\n4.Cathodic Arc Deposition employs a consumable cathode of the material which forms the coating and has an arc discharge established on the surface by a momentary contact of a ground trigger. Controlled motion of arcing erodes the cathode surface creating a highly ionized plasma. The anode can be either a cone attached to the periphery of the cathode, through an insulator, or the chamber. Substrate biasing is used for non line-of-sight deposition.\n\n\nN.B.This definition does not include random cathodic arc deposition with non-biased substrates.\n\n\n5.Ion Plating is a special modification of a general TE-PVD process in which a plasma or an ion source is used to ionize the species to be deposited, and a negative bias is applied to the substrate in order to facilitate the extraction of the species from the plasma. The introduction of reactive species, evaporation of solids within the process chamber, and the use of monitors to provide in-process measurement of optical characteristics and thicknesses of coatings are ordinary modifications of the process.\n\n\nc.Pack Cementation is a surface modification coating or overlay coating process wherein a substrate is immersed in a powder mixture (a pack), that consists of:\n\n\n1.The metallic powders that are to be deposited (usually aluminium, chromium, silicon or combinations thereof);\n\n\n2.An activator (normally a halide salt); and\n\n\n3.An inert powder, most frequently alumina.\n\n\nThe substrate and powder mixture is contained within a retort which is heated to between 1030 K (757 \u00b0C) and 1375 K (1,102 \u00b0C) for sufficient time to deposit the coating.\n\n\nd.Plasma Spraying is an overlay coating process wherein a gun (spray torch) which produces and controls a plasma accepts powder or wire coating materials, melts them and propels them towards a substrate, whereon an integrally bonded coating is formed. Plasma spraying constitutes either low pressure plasma spraying or high velocity plasma spraying.\n\n\nN.B. 1Low pressure means less than ambient atmospheric pressure.\n\n\n\n\nN.B. 2High velocity refers to nozzle-exit gas velocity exceeding 750 m/s calculated at 293 K (20 \u00b0C) at 0,1 MPa.\n\n\ne.Slurry Deposition is a surface modification coating or overlay coating process wherein a metallic or ceramic powder with an organic binder is suspended in a liquid and is applied to a substrate by either spraying, dipping or painting, subsequent air or oven drying, and heat treatment to obtain the desired coating.\n\n\nf.Sputter Deposition is an overlay coating process based on a momentum transfer phenomenon, wherein positive ions are accelerated by an electric field towards the surface of a target (coating material). The kinetic energy of the impacting ions is sufficient to cause target surface atoms to be released and deposited on an appropriately positioned substrate.\n\n\nN.B. 1The Table refers only to triode, magnetron or reactive sputter deposition which is used to increase adhesion of the coating and rate of deposition and to radio frequency (RF) augmented sputter deposition used to permit vaporisation of non-metallic coating materials.\n\n\nN.B. 2Low-energy ion beams (less than 5 keV) can be used to activate the deposition.\n\n\ng.Ion Implantation is a surface modification coating process in which the element to be alloyed is ionized, accelerated through a potential gradient and implanted into the surface region of the substrate. This includes processes in which ion implantation is performed simultaneously with electron beam physical vapour deposition or sputter deposition.\n\n\nCATEGORY 3 \u2014ELECTRONICS\n\n\n3ASystems, Equipment and Components\n\n\nNote 1:The control status of equipment and components described in 3A001 or 3A002, other than those described in 3A001.a.3. to 3A001.a.10., 3A001.a.12. or 3A001.a.13, which are specially designed for or which have the same functional characteristics as other equipment is determined by the control status of the other equipment.\n\n\nNote 2:The control status of integrated circuits described in 3A001.a.3. to 3A001.a.9., 3A001.a.12. or 3A001.a.13 Which are unalterably programmed or designed for a specific function for another equipment is determined by the control status of the other equipment.\n\n\nN.B.:When the manufacturer or applicant cannot determine the control status of the other equipment, the control status of the integrated circuits is determined in 3A001.a.3. to 3A001.a.9., 3A001.a.12 and 3A001.a.13.\n\n\n3A001\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Electronic components and specially designed components therefor, as follows:\n\n\na.General purpose integrated circuits, as follows:\n\n\nNote 1:The control status of wafers (finished or unfinished), in which the function has been determined, is to be evaluated against the parameters of 3A001.a.\n\n\nNote 2:Integrated circuits include the following types:\n\n\n\u2013\"Monolithic integrated circuits\";\n\n\n\u2013\"Hybrid integrated circuits\";\n\n\n\u2013\"Multichip integrated circuits\";\n\n\n\u2013\"Film type integrated circuits\", including silicon-on-sapphire integrated circuits;\n\n\n\u2013\"Optical integrated circuits\";\n\n\n\n\n\u2013\"Three dimensional integrated circuits\".\n\n\n1.Integrated circuits designed or rated as radiation hardened to withstand any of the following:\n\n\na.A total dose of 5 \u00d7 103 Gy (silicon) or higher;\n\n\nb.A dose rate upset of 5 \u00d7 106 Gy (silicon)/s or higher; or\n\n\nc.A fluence (integrated flux) of neutrons (1 MeV equivalent) of 5 \u00d7 1013 n/cm2 or higher on silicon, or its equivalent for other materials;\n\n\nNote:3A001.a.1.c. does not control Metal Insulator Semiconductors (MIS).\n\n\n2.\"Microprocessor microcircuits\", \"microcomputer microcircuits\", microcontroller microcircuits, storage integrated circuits manufactured from a compound semiconductor, analogue-to-digital converters, digital-to-analogue converters, electro-optical or \"optical integrated circuits\" designed for \"signal processing\", field programmable logic devices, custom integrated circuits for which either the function is unknown or the control status of the equipment in which the integrated circuit will be used is unknown, Fast Fourier Transform (FFT) processors, electrical erasable programmable read-only memories (EEPROMs), flash memories or static random-access memories (SRAMs), having any of the following:\n\n\na.Rated for operation at an ambient temperature above 398 K (125 \u00b0C);\n\n\nb.Rated for operation at an ambient temperature below 218 K (\u201355 \u00b0C); or\n\n\nc.Rated for operation over the entire ambient temperature range from 218 K (\u201355 \u00b0C) to 398 K (125 \u00b0C);\n\n\nNote:3A001.a.2. does not control integrated circuits for civil automobiles or railway train applications.\n\n\n3.\"Microprocessor microcircuits\", \"microcomputer microcircuits\" and microcontroller microcircuits, manufactured from a compound semiconductor and operating at a clock frequency exceeding 40 MHz;\n\n\nNote:3A001.a.3. includes digital signal processors, digital array processors and digital coprocessors.\n\n\n4.Not used;\n\n\n5.Analogue-to-Digital Converter (ADC) and Digital-to-Analogue Converter (DAC) integrated circuits, as follows:\n\n\na.ADCs having any of the following:\n\n\nN.B.:SEE ALSO 3A101\n\n\n1.A resolution of 8 bit or more, but less than 10 bit, with an output rate greater than 1,000 million words per second;\n\n\n2.A resolution of 10 bit or more, but less than 12 bit, with an output rate greater than 300 million words per second;\n\n\n3.A resolution of 12 bit with an output rate greater than 200 million words per second;\n\n\n\n\n4.A resolution of more than 12 bit, but equal to or less than 14 bit, with an output rate greater than 125 million words per second; or\n\n\n5.A resolution of more than 14 bit with an output rate greater than 20 million words per second;\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.A resolution of n bit corresponds to a quantisation of 2n levels.\n\n\n2.The number of bits in the output word is equal to the resolution of the ADC.\n\n\n3.The output rate is the maximum output rate of the converter, regardless of the architecture or oversampling.\n\n\n4.For 'multiple channel ADCs', the outputs are not aggregated and the output rate is the maximum output rate of any single channel.\n\n\n5.For 'interleaved ADCs' or for 'multiple channel ADCs' that are specified to have an interleaved mode of operation, the outputs are aggregated and the output rate is the maximum combined total output rate of all of the outputs.\n\n\n6.Vendors may also refer to the output rate as sampling rate, conversion rate or throughput rate. It is often specified in megahertz (MHz) or mega samples per second (MSPS).\n\n\n7.For the purpose of measuring output rate, one output word per second is equivalent to one Hertz or one sample per second.\n\n\n8.'Multiple channel ADCs' are defined as devices which integrate more than one ADC, designed so that each ADC has a separate analogue input.\n\n\n9.'Interleaved ADCs' are defined as devices which have multiple ADC units that sample the same analogue input at different times such that when the outputs are aggregated, the analogue input has been effectively sampled and converted at a higher sampling rate.\n\n\nb.Digital-to-Analogue Converters (DAC) having any of the following:\n\n\n1.A resolution of 10 bit or more with an 'adjusted update rate' of greater than 3500 MSPS; or\n\n\n2.\u00e81 A resolution of 12 bit or more with an 'adjusted update rate' of greater than 1250 MSPS and having any of the following: \u00e7\n\n\na.A settling time less than 9 ns to 0,024 % of full scale from a full scale step; or\n\n\nb.A 'Spurious Free Dynamic Range' (SFDR) greater than 68 dBc (carrier) when synthesising a full scale analogue signal of 100 MHz or the highest full scale analogue signal frequency specified below 100 MHz.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.'Spurious Free Dynamic Range' (SFDR) is defined as the ratio of the RMS value of the carrier frequency (maximum signal component) at the input of the DAC to the RMS value of the next largest noise or harmonic distortion component at its output.\n\n\n2.SFDR is determined directly from the specification table or from the characterisation plots of SFDR versus frequency.\n\n\n\n\n3.A signal is defined to be full scale when its amplitude is greater than \u2013 3 dBfs (full scale).\n\n\n4.'Adjusted update rate' for DACs:\n\n\na.For conventional (non-interpolating) DACs, the 'adjusted update rate' is the rate at which the digital signal is converted to an analogue signal and the output analogue values are changed by the DAC. For DACs where the interpolation mode may be bypassed (interpolation factor of one), the DAC should be considered as a conventional (non-interpolating) DAC.\n\n\nb.For interpolating DACs (oversampling DACs), the 'adjusted update rate' is defined as the DAC update rate divided by the smallest interpolating factor. For interpolating DACs, the 'adjusted update rate' may be referred to by different terms including:\n\n\n\u2013input data rate\n\n\n\u2013input word rate\n\n\n\u2013input sample rate\n\n\n\u2013maximum total input bus rate\n\n\n\u2013maximum DAC clock rate for DAC clock input.\n\n\n6.Electro-optical and \"optical integrated circuits\", designed for \"signal processing\" and having all of the following:\n\n\na.One or more than one internal \"laser\" diode;\n\n\nb.One or more than one internal light detecting element; and\n\n\nc.Optical waveguides;\n\n\n7.'Field programmable logic devices' having any of the following:\n\n\na.A maximum number of single-ended digital input/outputs of greater than 700; or\n\n\nb.An 'aggregate one-way peak serial transceiver data rate' of 500 Gb/s or greater;\n\n\nNote:3A001.a.7. includes:\n\n\n\u2013Simple Programmable Logic Devices (SPLDs)\n\n\n\u2013Complex Programmable Logic Devices (CPLDs)\n\n\n\u2013Field Programmable Gate Arrays (FPGAs)\n\n\n\n\n\u2013Field Programmable Logic Arrays (FPLAs)\n\n\n\u2013Field Programmable Interconnects (FPICs)\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.Maximum number of digital input/outputs in 3A001.a.7.a. is also referred to as the maximum user input/outputs or maximum available input/outputs, whether the integrated circuit is packaged or bare die.\n\n\n2.'Aggregate one-way peak serial transceiver data rate' is the product of the peak serial one-way transceiver data rate times the number of transceivers on the FPGA.\n\n\n8.Not used;\n\n\n9.Neural network integrated circuits;\n\n\n10.Custom integrated circuits for which the function is unknown, or the control status of the equipment in which the integrated circuits will be used is unknown to the manufacturer, having any of the following:\n\n\na.More than 1500 terminals;\n\n\nb.A typical \"basic gate propagation delay time\" of less than 0,02 ns; or\n\n\nc.An operating frequency exceeding 3 GHz;\n\n\n11.Digital integrated circuits, other than those described in 3A001.a.3. to 3A001.a.10. and 3A001.a.12., based upon any compound semiconductor and having any of the following:\n\n\na.An equivalent gate count of more than 3000 (2 input gates); or\n\n\nb.A toggle frequency exceeding 1,2 GHz;\n\n\n12.Fast Fourier Transform (FFT) processors having a rated execution time for an N-point complex FFT of less than (N log2 N) /20480 ms, where N is the number of points;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nWhen N is equal to 1,024 points, the formula in 3A001.a.12. gives an execution time of 500 \u03bcs.\n\n\n13.Direct Digital Synthesizer (DDS) integrated circuits having any of the following:\n\n\na.A Digital-to-Analogue Converter (DAC) clock frequency of 3,5 GHz or more and a DAC resolution of 10 bit or more, but less than 12 bit; or\n\n\nb.A DAC clock frequency of 1,25 GHz or more and a DAC resolution of 12 bit or more;\n\n\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nThe DAC clock frequency may be specified as the master clock frequency or the input clock frequency\n\n\nb.Microwave or millimetre wave components, as follows:\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nFor purposes of 3A001.b., the parameter peak saturated power output may also be referred to on product data sheets as output power, saturated power output, maximum power output, peak power output, or peak envelope power output.\n\n\n1.Electronic vacuum tubes and cathodes, as follows:\n\n\nNote 1:3A001.b.1. does not control tubes designed or rated for operation in any frequency band and having all of the following:\n\n\na.Does not exceed 31,8 GHz; and\n\n\n3.Any two sides perpendicular to one another with either length d (in cm) equal to or less than 15 divided by the lowest operating frequency in GHz [d \u2264 15 cm*GHz/ fGHz];\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n\n\n2.7 GHz should be used as the lowest operating frequency (fGHz) in the formula in 3A001.b.4.f.3., for amplifiers that have a rated operating range extending downward to 2.7 GHz and below [d \u2264 15 cm*GHz/2,7 GHz].\n\n\nN.B.:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0MMIC power amplifiers should be evaluated against the criteria in 3A001.b.2.\n\n\nNote 1:Not used.\n\n\nNote 2:The control status of an item whose rated operating frequency includes frequencies listed in more than one frequency range, as defined by 3A001.b.4.a. to 3A001.b.4.e., is determined by the lowest peak saturation output threshold.\n\n\nNote 3:3A001.b.4. includes transmit/receive modules and transmit modules.\n\n\n5.Electronically or magnetically tunable band-pass or band-stop filters, having more than 5 tunable resonators capable of tuning across a 1,5:1 frequency band (fmax/fmin) in less than 10 \u03bcs and having any of the following:\n\n\na.A band-pass bandwidth of more than 0,5 % of centre frequency; or\n\n\nb.A band-stop bandwidth of less than 0,5 % of centre frequency;\n\n\n6.Not used;\n\n\n7.Converters and harmonic mixers that are any of the following:\n\n\na.Designed to extend the frequency range of \"signal analysers\" beyond 90 GHz;\n\n\nb.Designed to extend the operating range of signal generators as follows:\n\n\n1.Beyond 90 GHz;\n\n\n2.To an output power greater than 100 mW (20 dBm) anywhere within the frequency range exceeding 43.5 GHz but not exceeding 90 GHz;\n\n\nc.Designed to extend the operating range of network analysers as follows:\n\n\n1.Beyond 110 GHz;\n\n\n2.To an output power greater than 31.62 mW (15 dBm) anywhere within the frequency range exceeding 43.5 GHz but not exceeding 90 GHz;\n\n\n3.To an output power greater than 1 mW (0 dBm) anywhere within the frequency range exceeding 90 GHz but not exceeding 110 GHz; or\n\n\nd.Designed to extend the frequency range of microwave test receivers beyond 110 GHz;\n\n\n8.Microwave power amplifiers containing tubes specified in 3A001.b.1. and having all of the following: \n\n\n\n\na.Operating frequencies above 3 GHz;\n\n\nb.An average output power to mass ratio exceeding 80 W/kg; or\n\n\n2.Frequency selection at all frequencies using resonant circuits with Q-values exceeding 10000;\n\n\ne.High energy devices as follows:\n\n\n1.'Cells' as follows:\n\n\na.'Primary cells' having an 'energy density' exceeding 550 Wh/kg at 20 \u00b0C;\n\n\nb.'Secondary cells' having an 'energy density' exceeding 300 Wh/kg at 20 \u00b0C;\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.For the purpose of 3A001.e.1.,'energy density' (Wh/kg) is calculated from the nominal voltage multiplied by the nominal capacity in ampere-hours (Ah) divided by the mass in kilograms. If the nominal capacity is not stated, energy density is calculated from the nominal voltage squared then multiplied by the discharge duration in hours divided by the discharge load in ohms and the mass in kilograms.\n\n\n2.For the purpose of 3A001.e.1., a 'cell' is defined as an electrochemical device, which has positive and negative electrodes, an electrolyte, and is a source of electrical energy. It is the basic building block of a battery.\n\n\n3.For the purpose of 3A001.e.1.a., a 'primary cell' is a 'cell' that is not designed to be charged by any other source.\n\n\n4.For the purpose of 3A001.e.1.b., a 'secondary cell' is a 'cell' that is designed to be charged by an external electrical source.\n\n\nNote:3A001.e.1. does not control batteries, including single-cell batteries.\n\n\n2.High energy storage capacitors as follows:\n\n\nN.BSEE ALSO 3A201.a. and the Military Goods Controls.\n\n\na.Capacitors with a repetition rate of less than 10 Hz (single shot capacitors) and having all of the following:\n\n\n1.A voltage rating equal to or more than 5 kV;\n\n\n2.An energy density equal to or more than 250 J/kg; If the accelerator beam pulse duration is greater than 1 \u03bcs, then Q is the maximum accelerated charge in 1 \u03bcs.\n\n\nQ equals the integral of i with respect to t, over the lesser of 1 \u03bcs or the time duration of the beam pulse (Q = \u222b idt), where i is beam current in amperes and t is time in seconds.\n\n\n2.'Peak power' = (peak potential in volts) \u00d7 (peak beam current in amperes).\n\n\n3.In machines based on microwave accelerating cavities, the time duration of the beam pulse is the lesser of 1 \u03bcs or the duration of the bunched beam packet resulting from one microwave modulator pulse.\n\n\n4.In machines based on microwave accelerating cavities, the peak beam current is the average current in the time duration of a bunched beam packet.\n\n\n3A225\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Frequency changers or generators, other than those specified in 0B001.b.13., usable as a variable or fixed frequency motor drive, having all of the following characteristics:\n\n\nN.B. 1:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Software\" specially designed to enhance or release the performance of a frequency changer or generator to meet the characteristics of 3A225 is specified in 3D225.\n\n\nN.B. 2:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Technology\" in the form of codes or keys to enhance or release the performance of a frequency changer or generator to meet the characteristics of 3A225 is specified in 3E225.\n\n\na.Multiphase output providing a power of 40 VA or greater;\n\n\nb.Operating at a frequency of 600 Hz or more; and\n\n\n2.Rated for a peak current of 500 A or more;\n\n\nc.Modules or assemblies with a fast switching function, other than those specified in 3A001.g. or 3A001.h., having all of the following characteristics:\n\n\n\n\n1.Anode peak voltage rating greater than 2 kV;\n\n\n2.Anode peak current rating of 500 A or more; and\n\n\n3.Turn-on time of 1 \u03bcs or less.\n\n\n3A229\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0High-current pulse generators as follows:\n\n\nN.B.:SEE ALSO MILITARY GOODS CONTROLS.\n\n\na.Detonator firing sets (initiator systems, firesets), including electronically-charged, explosively-driven and optically-driven firing sets, other than those specified in 1A007.a., designed to drive multiple controlled detonators specified in 1A007.b.;\n\n\nb.Modular electrical pulse generators (pulsers) having all of the following characteristics:\n\n\n1.Designed for portable, mobile, or ruggedized-use;\n\n\n2.Capable of delivering their energy in less than 15 \u03bcs into loads of less than 40 ohms;\n\n\n3.Having an output greater than 100 A;\n\n\n4.No dimension greater than 30 cm;\n\n\n5.Weight less than 30 kg; and\n\n\n6.Specified for use over an extended temperature range 223 K (\u201350 \u00b0C) to 373 K (100 \u00b0C) or specified as suitable for aerospace applications.\n\n\nNote:3A229.b. includes xenon flash-lamp drivers.\n\n\nc.Micro-firing units having all of the following characteristics:\n\n\n1.No dimension greater than 35 mm;\n\n\n2.Voltage rating of equal to or greater than 1 kV; and\n\n\n3.Capacitance of equal to or greater than 100 nF.\n\n\n3A230\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0High-speed pulse generators, and 'pulse heads' therefor, having both of the following characteristics:\n\n\na.Output voltage greater than 6 V into a resistive load of less than 55 ohms, and\n\n\n\n\nb.'Pulse transition time' less than 500 ps.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.In 3A230, 'pulse transition time' is defined as the time interval between 10 % and 90 % voltage amplitude.\n\n\n2.'Pulse heads' are impulse forming networks designed to accept a voltage step function and shape it into a variety of pulse forms that can include rectangular, triangular, step, impulse, exponential, or monocycle types. 'Pulse heads' can be an integral part of the pulse generator, they can be a plug-in module to the device or they can be an externally connected device.\n\n\n3A231\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Neutron generator systems, including tubes, having both of the following characteristics:\n\n\na.Designed for operation without an external vacuum system; and\n\n\nb.Utilizing any of the following:\n\n\n1.Electrostatic acceleration to induce a tritium-deuterium nuclear reaction; or\n\n\n2.Electrostatic acceleration to induce a deuterium-deuterium nuclear reaction and capable of an output of 3 \u00d7 109 neutrons/s or greater.\n\n\n3A232\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Multipoint initiation systems, other than those specified in 1A007, as follows:\n\n\nN.B.:SEE ALSO MILITARY GOODS CONTROLS.\n\n\nN.B.:See 1A007.b. for detonators.\n\n\na.Not used;\n\n\nb.Arrangements using single or multiple detonators designed to nearly simultaneously initiate an explosive surface over greater than 5,000 mm2 from a single firing signal with an initiation timing spread over the surface of less than 2,5 \u03bcs.\n\n\nNote:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a03A232 does not control detonators using only primary explosives, such as lead azide.\n\n\n3A233\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Mass spectrometers, other than those specified in 0B002.g., capable of measuring ions of 230 atomic mass units or greater and having a resolution of better than 2 parts in 230, as follows, and ion sources therefor:\n\n\na.Inductively coupled plasma mass spectrometers (ICP/MS);\n\n\nb.Glow discharge mass spectrometers (GDMS);\n\n\nc.Thermal ionization mass spectrometers (TIMS);\n\n\nd.Electron bombardment mass spectrometers having both of the following features:\n\n\n\n\n1.A molecular beam inlet system that injects a collimated beam of analyte molecules into a region of the ion source where the molecules are ionized by an electron beam; and\n\n\n2.One or more 'cold traps' that can be cooled to a temperature of 193 K (\u201380 \u00b0C);\n\n\ne.Not used;\n\n\nf.Mass spectrometers equipped with a microfluorination ion source designed for actinides or actinide fluorides.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.Electron bombardment mass spectrometers in 3A233.d. are also known as electron impact mass spectrometers or electron ionization mass spectrometers.\n\n\n2.In 3A233.d.2., a 'cold trap' is a device that traps gas molecules by condensing or freezing them on cold surfaces. For the purposes of 3A233.d.2., a closed-loop gaseous helium cryogenic vacuum pump is not a 'cold trap'.\n\n\n3A234\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Striplines to provide low inductance path to detonators with the following characteristics:\n\n\na.Voltage rating greater than 2 kV; and\n\n\nb.Inductance of less than 20 nH.\n\n\n3BTest, Inspection and Production Equipment\n\n\n3B001\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Equipment for the manufacturing of semiconductor devices or materials, as follows and specially designed components and accessories therefor:\n\n\na.Equipment designed for epitaxial growth as follows:\n\n\n1.Equipment capable of producing a layer of any material other than silicon with a thickness uniform to less than \u00b1 2,5 % across a distance of 75 mm or more;\n\n\nNote:3B001.a.1. includes Atomic Layer Epitaxy (ALE) equipment.\n\n\n2.Metal Organic Chemical Vapour Deposition (MOCVD) reactors designed for compound semiconductor epitaxial growth of material having two or more of the following elements: aluminium, gallium, indium, arsenic, phosphorus, antimony, or nitrogen;\n\n\n3.Molecular beam epitaxial growth equipment using gas or solid sources;\n\n\nb.Equipment designed for ion implantation and having any of the following:\n\n\n1.Not used;\n\n\n2.Being designed and optimized to operate at a beam energy of 20 keV or more and a beam current of 10 mA or more for hydrogen, deuterium or helium implant;\n\n\n\n\n3.Direct write capability;\n\n\n4.A beam energy of 65 keV or more and a beam current of 45 mA or more for high energy oxygen implant into a heated semiconductor material \"substrate\"; or\n\n\n5.Being designed and optimized to operate at a beam energy of 20 keV or more and a beam current of 10 mA or more for silicon implant into a semiconductor material \"substrate\" heated to 600 \u00b0C or greater;\n\n\nc.Anisotropic plasma dry etching equipment having all of the following:\n\n\n1.Designed or optimised to produce critical dimensions of 65 nm or less; and\n\n\n2.Within-wafer non-uniformity equal to or less than 10 % 3\u03c3 measured with an edge exclusion of 2 mm or less;\n\n\nd.Not used;\n\n\ne.Automatic loading multi-chamber central wafer handling systems having all of the following:\n\n\n1.Interfaces for wafer input and output, to which more than two functionally different 'semiconductor process tools' specified in 3B001.a., 3B001.b. or 3B001.c. are designed to be connected; and\n\n\n2.Designed to form an integrated system in a vacuum environment for 'sequential multiple wafer processing';\n\n\nNote:3B001.e. does not control automatic robotic wafer handling systems specially designed for parallel wafer processing.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.For the purpose of 3B001.e., 'semiconductor process tools' refers to modular tools that provide physical processes for semiconductor production that are functionally different, such as deposition, etch, implant or thermal processing.\n\n\n2.For the purpose of 3B001.e., 'sequential multiple wafer processing' means the capability to process each wafer in different 'semiconductor process tools', such as by transferring each wafer from one tool to a second tool and on to a third tool with the automatic loading multi-chamber central wafer handling systems.\n\n\nf.Lithography equipment as follows:\n\n\n1.Align and expose step and repeat (direct step on wafer) or step and scan (scanner) equipment for wafer processing using photo-optical or X-ray methods and having any of the following:\n\n\na.A light source wavelength shorter than 193 nm; or\n\n\nb.Capable of producing a pattern with a 'Minimum Resolvable Feature size' (MRF) of 45 nm or less;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nThe 'Minimum Resolvable Feature size' (MRF) is calculated by the following formula:\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nMRF = (an exposure light source wavelength in nm) x (K factor)\n\n\n\n\n\n\nnumerical aperture\n\n\n\n\n\n\nwhere the K factor = 0,35\n\n\n2.Imprint lithography equipment capable of producing features of 45 nm or less;\n\n\nNote:3B001.f.2. includes:\n\n\n\u2013Micro contact printing tools\n\n\n\u2013Hot embossing tools\n\n\n\u2013Nano-imprint lithography tools\n\n\n\u2013Step and flash imprint lithography (S-FIL) tools\n\n\n3.Equipment specially designed for mask making or semiconductor device processing using direct writing methods, having all of the following:\n\n\na.Using deflected focussed electron beam, ion beam or \"laser\" beam; and\n\n\nb.Having any of the following:\n\n\n1.A spot size smaller than 0,2 \u03bcm;\n\n\n2.Being capable of producing a pattern with a feature size of less than 1 \u03bcm; or\n\n\n3.An overlay accuracy of better than \u00b1 0,20 \u03bcm (3 sigma);\n\n\ng.Masks and reticles, designed for integrated circuits specified in 3A001;\n\n\nh.Multi-layer masks with a phase shift layer not specified by 3B001.g. and having any of the following:\n\n\n1.Made on a mask \"substrate blank\" from glass specified as having less than 7 nm/cm birefringence; or\n\n\n2.Designed to be used by lithography equipment having a light source wavelength less than 245 nm;\n\n\nNote:3B001.h. does not control multi-layer masks with a phase shift layer designed for the fabrication of memory devices not controlled by 3A001.\n\n\n\n\ni.Imprint lithography templates designed for integrated circuits specified in 3A001.\n\n\n3B002\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Test equipment specially designed for testing finished or unfinished semiconductor devices as follows and specially designed components and accessories therefor:\n\n\na.For testing S-parameters of transistor devices at frequencies exceeding 31,8 GHz;\n\n\nb.Not used;\n\n\nc.For testing microwave integrated circuits specified in 3A001.b.2.\n\n\n3CMaterials\n\n\n3C001\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Hetero-epitaxial materials consisting of a \"substrate\" having stacked epitaxially grown multiple layers of any of the %;\n\n\nb.Organo-arsenic, organo-antimony and organo-phosphorus compounds, having a purity (inorganic element basis) better than 99,999 %.\n\n\nNote:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a03C003 only controls compounds or 3C;\n\n\n\n\nNote 1:3E001 does not control \"technology\" for the \"production\" of equipment or components controlled by 3A003.\n\n\nNote 2:3E001 does not control \"technology\" for the \"development\" or \"production\" of integrated circuits specified in 3A001.a.3. to 3A001.a.12., having all of the following:\n\n\na.Using \"technology\" at or above 0.130 \u03bcm; and\n\n\nb.Incorporating multi-layer structures with three or fewer metal layers.\n\n\n3E002\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Technology\" according to the General Technology Note, other than that specified in 3E001, for the \"development\" or \"production\" of a \"microprocessor microcircuit\", \"microcomputer microcircuit\" or microcontroller microcircuit core, having an arithmetic logic unit with an access width of 32 bits or more and any of the following features or characteristics:\n\n\na.A 'vector processor unit' designed to perform more than two calculations on floating-point vectors (one-dimensional arrays of 32-bit or larger numbers) simultaneously;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nA 'vector processor unit' is a processor element with built-in instructions that perform multiple calculations on floating-point vectors (one-dimensional arrays of 32-bit or larger numbers) simultaneously, having at least one vector arithmetic logic unit.\n\n\nb.Designed to perform more than four 64-bit or larger floating-point operation results per cycle; or\n\n\nc.Designed to perform more than four 16-bit fixed-point multiply-accumulate results per cycle (e.g., digital manipulation of analogue information that has been previously converted into digital form, also known as digital \"signal processing\").\n\n\nNote:3E002.c. does not control \"technology\" for multimedia extensions.\n\n\nNote 1:3E002 does not control \"technology\" for the \"development\" or \"production\" of micro-processor cores, having all of the following:\n\n\na.Using \"technology\" at or above 0.130 \u03bcm; and\n\n\nb.Incorporating multi-layer structures with five or fewer metal layers.\n\n\nNote 2:3E002 includes \"technology\" for digital signal processors and digital array processors.\n\n\n3E003\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Other \"technology\" for the \"development\" or \"production\" of the following:\n\n\na.Vacuum microelectronic devices;\n\n\nb.Hetero-structure semiconductor electronic devices such as high electron mobility transistors (HEMT), hetero-bipolar transistors (HBT), quantum well and super lattice devices;\n\n\nNote:3E003.b. does not control \"technology\" for high electron mobility transistors (HEMT) operating at frequencies lower than 31,8 GHz and hetero-junction bipolar transistors (HBT) operating at frequencies lower than 31,8 GHz.\n\n\nc.\"Superconductive\" electronic devices;\n\n\n\n\nd.Substrates of films of diamond for electronic components.\n\n\ne.Substrates of silicon-on-insulator (SOI) for integrated circuits in which the insulator is silicon dioxide;\n\n\nf.Substrates of silicon carbide for electronic components;\n\n\ng.Electronic vacuum tubes operating at frequencies of 31,8 GHz or higher.\n\n\n3E101\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Technology\" according to the General Technology Note for the \"use\" of equipment or \"software\" specified in 3A001.a.1. or 2., 3A101, 3A102 or 3D101.\n\n\n3E102\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Technology\" according to the General Technology Note for the \"development\" of \"software\" specified in 3D101.\n\n\n3E201\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Technology\" according to the General Technology Note for the \"use\" of equipment specified in 3A001.e.2., 3A001.e.3., 3A001.g., 3A201, 3A225 to 3A234.\n\n\n3E225\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Technology\", in the form of codes or keys, to enhance or release the performance of frequency changers or generators to meet the characteristics of 3A225.\n\n\nCATEGORY 4 \u2014COMPUTERS\n\n\nNote 1:Computers, related equipment and \"software\" performing telecommunications or \"local area network\" functions must also be evaluated against the performance characteristics of Category 5, Part 1 (Telecommunications).\n\n\nNote 2:Control units which directly interconnect the buses or channels of central processing units, \"main storage\" or disk controllers are not regarded as telecommunications equipment described in Category 5, Part 1 (Telecommunications).\n\n\nN.B.:For the control status of \"software\" specially designed for packet switching, see 5D001.\n\n\nNote 3:Computers, related equipment and \"software\" performing cryptographic, cryptanalytic, certifiable multi-level security or certifiable user isolation functions, or which limit electromagnetic compatibility (EMC), must also be evaluated against the performance characteristics in Category 5, Part 2 (\"Information Security\").\n\n\n4ASystems, Equipment and Components\n\n\n4A001\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Electronic computers and related equipment, Error/bit/day;\n\n\n\n\n\n\nNote:4A001.a.2. does not control computers specially designed for \"civil aircraft\" applications.\n\n\nb.Not used.\n\n\n4A003\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Digital computers\", \"production\" or \"use\" of equipment or \"software\" specified in 4A or 4D.\n\n\nb.\"Technology\", other than that specified in 4E001.a., specially designed or modified for the \"development\" or \"production\" of equipment as follows:\n\n\n1.\"Digital computers\" having an \"Adjusted Peak Performance\" (\"APP\") exceeding 1,0 weighted TeraFLOPS (WT);\n\n\n2.\"Electronic assemblies\" specially designed or modified for enhancing performance by aggregation of processors so that the \"APP\" of the aggregation exceeds the limit in 4E001.b.1.\n\n\nc.\"Technology\" for the \"development\" of \"intrusion software\".\n\n\nTECHNICAL NOTE ON \"ADJUSTED PEAK PERFORMANCE\" (\"APP\")\n\n\n\"APP\" is an adjusted peak rate at which \"digital computers\" perform 64-bit or larger floating point additions and multiplications.\n\n\n\"APP\" is expressed in Weighted TeraFLOPS (WT), in units of 1012 adjusted floating point operations per second\n\n\n\n\nAbbreviations used in this Technical Note\n\n\n\n\n\nn\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nnumber of processors in the \"digital computer\"\n\n\n\n\n\n\ni\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nprocessor number (i,\u2026n)\n\n\n\n\n\n\nti\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nprocessor cycle time (ti = 1/Fi)\n\n\n\n\n\n\nFi\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nprocessor frequency\n\n\n\n\n\n\nRi\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\npeak floating point calculating rate\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWi\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\narchitecture adjustment factor\n\n\n\n\n\n\nOutline of \"APP\" calculation method\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0For each processor i, determine the peak number of 64-bit or larger floating point operations, FPOi, performed per cycle for each processor in the \"digital computer\".\n\n\nNote\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0In determining FPO, include only 64-bit or larger floating point additions and/or multiplications. All floating point operations must be expressed in operations per processor cycle; operations requiring multiple cycles may be expressed in fractional results per cycle. For processors not capable of performing calculations on floating point operands of 64-bit or more, the effective calculating rate R is zero.\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Calculate the floating point rate R for each processor Ri = FPOi/ti.\n\n\n3.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Calculate \"APP\" as \"APP\" = W1 \u00d7 R1 + W2 \u00d7 R2 + \u2026 + Wn \u00d7 Rn.\n\n\n4.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0For 'vector processors', Wi = 0,9. For non-'vector processors', Wi = 0,3.\n\n\nNote 1For processors that perform compound operations in a cycle, such as addition and multiplication, each operation is counted.\n\n\nNote 2For a pipelined processor the effective calculating rate R is the faster of the pipelined rate, once the pipeline is full, or the non-pipelined rate.\n\n\nNote 3The calculating rate R of each contributing processor is to be calculated at its maximum value theoretically possible before the \"APP\" of the combination is derived. Simultaneous operations are assumed to exist when the computer manufacturer claims concurrent, parallel, or simultaneous operation or execution in a manual or brochure for the computer.\n\n\nNote 4Do not include processors that are limited to input/output and peripheral functions (e.g., disk drive, communication and video display) when calculating \"APP\".\n\n\nNote 5\"APP\" values are not to be calculated for processor combinations (inter)connected by \"Local Area Networks\", Wide Area Networks, I/O shared connections/devices, I/O controllers and any communication interconnection implemented by \"software\".\n\n\nNote 6\"APP\" values must be calculated for processor combinations containing processors specially designed to enhance performance by aggregation, operating simultaneously and sharing memory;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n1.Aggregate all processors and accelerators operating simultaneously and located on the same die.\n\n\n2.Processor combinations share memory when any processor is capable of accessing any memory location in the system through the hardware transmission of cache lines or memory words, without the involvement of any software mechanism, which may be achieved using \"electronic assemblies\" specified in 4A003.c.\n\n\nNote 7A 'vector processor' is defined as a processor with built-in instructions that perform multiple calculations on floating-point vectors (one-dimensional arrays of 64-bit or larger numbers) simultaneously, having at least 2 vector functional units and at least 8 vector registers of at least 64 elements each.\n\n\nCATEGORY 5 \u2014TELECOMMUNICATIONS AND \"INFORMATION SECURITY\"\n\n\n\n\nPART 1 \u2014TELECOMMUNICATIONS\n\n\nNote 1:The control status of components, \"lasers\", test and \"production\" equipment and \"software\", therefor which are specially designed for telecommunications equipment or systems is determined in Category 5, Part 1.\n\n\nN.B. 1:For \"lasers\" specially designed for telecommunications equipment or systems, see 6A005.\n\n\nN.B. 2:See also Category 5, Part 2 for equipment, components, and \"software\", performing or incorporating \"information security\" functions.\n\n\nNote 2:\"Digital computers\", related equipment or \"software\", when essential for the operation and support of telecommunications equipment described in this Category, are regarded as specially designed components, provided they are the standard models customarily supplied by the manufacturer. This includes operation, administration, maintenance, engineering or billing computer systems.\n\n\n5A1Systems, Equipment and Components\n\n\n5A001\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Telecommunications systems, equipment, components and accessories as follows:\n\n\na.Any type of telecommunications equipment having any of the following characteristics, functions or features:\n\n\n1.Specially designed to withstand transitory electronic effects or electromagnetic pulse effects, both arising from a nuclear explosion;\n\n\n2.Specially hardened to withstand gamma, neutron or ion radiation; or\n\n\n3.Specially designed to operate outside the temperature range from 218 K (\u201355 \u00b0C) to 397 K (124 \u00b0C);\n\n\nNote:5A001.a.3. applies only to electronic equipment.\n\n\nNote:5A001.a.2. and 5A001.a.3. do not control equipment designed or modified for use on board satellites.\n\n\nb.Telecommunication systems and equipment, and specially designed components and accessories therefor, having any of the following characteristics, functions or features:\n\n\n1.Being underwater untethered communications systems having any of the following:\n\n\na.An acoustic carrier frequency outside the range from 20 kHz to 60 kHz;\n\n\nb.Using an electromagnetic carrier frequency below 30 kHz;\n\n\nc.Using electronic beam steering techniques; or\n\n\nd.Using \"lasers\" or light-emitting diodes (LEDs) with an output wavelength greater than 400 nm and less than 700 nm, in a \"local area network\";\n\n\n2.Being radio equipment operating in the 1,5 MHz to 87,5 MHz band and having all of the following:\n\n\n\n\na.Automatically predicting and selecting frequencies and \"total digital transfer rates\" per channel to optimise the transmission; and\n\n\nb.Incorporating a linear power amplifier configuration having a capability to support multiple signals simultaneously at an output power of 1 kW or more in the frequency range of 1,5 MHz or more but less than 30 MHz, or 250 W or more in the frequency range of 30 MHz or more but not exceeding 87,5 MHz, over an \"instantaneous bandwidth\" of one octave or more and with an output harmonic and distortion content of better than -80 dB;\n\n\n3.Being radio equipment employing \"spread spectrum\" techniques, including \"frequency hopping\" techniques, other than those specified in 5A001.b.4. and having any of the following:\n\n\na.User programmable spreading codes; or\n\n\nb.A total transmitted bandwidth which is 100 or more times the bandwidth of any one information channel and in excess of 50 kHz; \n\n\nNote:5A001.b.3.b. does not control radio equipment specially designed for use with any of the following:\n\n\na.Civil cellular radio-communications systems; or\n\n\nb.Fixed or mobile satellite earth stations for commercial civil telecommunications.\n\n\nNote:5A001.b.3 does not control equipment designed to operate at an output power of 1 W or less.\n\n\n4.Being radio equipment employing ultra-wideband modulation techniques, having user programmable channelising codes, scrambling codes or network identification codes and having any of the following:\n\n\na.A bandwidth exceeding 500 MHz; or\n\n\nb.A \"fractional bandwidth\" of 20 % or more;\n\n\n5.Being digitally controlled radio receivers having all of the following:\n\n\na.More than 1000 channels;\n\n\nb.A 'channel switching time' of less than 1 ms;\n\n\nc.Automatic searching or scanning of a part of the electromagnetic spectrum; and\n\n\nd.Identification of the received signals or the type of transmitter; or\n\n\nNote:5A001.b.5. does not control radio equipment specially designed for use with civil cellular radio-communications systems.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n'Channel switching time' means the time (i.e., delay) to change from one receiving frequency to another, to arrive at or within \u00b1 0,05 % of the final specified receiving frequency. Items having a specified frequency range of less than \u00b1 0.05 % around their centre frequency are defined to be incapable of channel frequency switching.\n\n\n\n\n6.Employing functions of digital \"signal processing\" to provide 'voice coding' output at rates of less than 2400 bit/s.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.For variable rate 'voice coding', 5A001.b.6. applies to the 'voice coding' output of continuous speech.\n\n\n2.For the purposes of 5A001.b.6., 'voice coding' is defined as the technique to take samples of human voice and then convert these samples into a digital signal, taking into account specific characteristics of human speech.\n\n\nc.Optical fibres of more than 500 m in length and specified by the manufacturer as being capable of withstanding a 'proof test' tensile stress of 2 \u00d7 109 N/m2 or more; \n\n\nN.B.:For underwater umbilical cables, see 8A002.a.3.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Proof Test': on-line or off-line production screen testing that dynamically applies a prescribed tensile stress over a 0,5 to 3 m length of fibre at a running rate of 2 to 5 m/s while passing between capstans approximately 150 mm in diameter. The ambient temperature is a nominal 293 K (20 \u00b0C) and relative humidity 40 %. Equivalent national standards may be used for executing the proof test.\n\n\nd.\"Electronically steerable phased array antennae\" operating above 31,8 GHz;\n\n\nNote:5A001.d. does not control \"electronically steerable phased array antennae\" for landing systems with instruments meeting ICAO standards covering Microwave Landing Systems (MLS).\n\n\ne.Radio direction finding equipment operating at frequencies above 30 MHz and having all of the following, and specially designed components therefor:\n\n\n1.\"Instantaneous bandwidth\" of 10 MHz or more; and\n\n\n2.Capable of finding a Line Of Bearing (LOB) to non-cooperating radio transmitters with a signal duration of less than 1 ms;\n\n\nf.Mobile telecommunications interception or jamming equipment, and monitoring equipment therefor, as follows, and specially designed components therefor:\n\n\n1.Interception equipment designed for the extraction of voice or data, transmitted over the air interface;\n\n\n2.Interception equipment not specified in 5A001.f.1., designed for the extraction of client device or subscriber identifiers (e.g., IMSI, TIMSI or IMEI), signalling, or other metadata transmitted over the air interface;\n\n\n3.Jamming equipment specially designed or modified to intentionally and selectively interfere with, deny, inhibit, degrade or seduce mobile telecommunication services and performing any of the following:\n\n\na.Simulate the functions of Radio Access Network (RAN) equipment;\n\n\nb.Detect and exploit specific characteristics of the mobile telecommunications protocol employed (e.g., GSM); or\n\n\nc.Exploit specific characteristics of the mobile telecommunications protocol employed (e.g. GSM);\n\n\n\n\n4.RF monitoring equipment designed or modified to identify the operation of items specified in 5A001.f.1., 5A001.f.2. or 5A001.f.3.; \n\n\nNote:5A001.f.1. and 5A001.f.2. do not control any of the following:\n\n\na.Equipment specially designed for the interception of analogue Private Mobile Radio (PMR), IEEE 802.11 WLAN;\n\n\nb.Equipment designed for mobile telecommunications network operators; or\n\n\nc.Equipment designed for the \"development\" or \"production\" of mobile telecommunications equipment or systems.\n\n\nN.B. 1.:See also MILITARY GOODS CONTROLS.\n\n\nN.B. 2.:For radio receivers see 5A001.b.5.\n\n\ng.Passive Coherent Location (PCL) systems or equipment, specially designed for detecting and tracking moving objects by measuring reflections of ambient radio frequency emissions, supplied by non-radar transmitters;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nNon-radar transmitters may include commercial radio, television or cellular telecommunications base stations.\n\n\nNote:5A001.g. does not control any of the following:\n\n\na.Radio-astronomical equipment; or\n\n\nb.Systems or equipment, that require any radio transmission from the target.\n\n\nh.Counter Improvised Explosive Device (IED) equipment and related equipment, as follows:\n\n\n1.Radio Frequency (RF) transmitting equipment, not specified in 5A001.f., designed or modified for prematurely activating or preventing the initiation of Improvised Explosive Devices;\n\n\n2.Equipment using techniques designed to enable radio communications in the same frequency channels on which co-located equipment specified in 5A001.h.1. is transmitting.\n\n\nN.B.:See also MILITARY GOODS CONTROLS.\n\n\ni.Not used;\n\n\nj.Internet Protocol (IP) network communications surveillance systems or equipment, and specially designed components therefor, having all of the following:\n\n\n1.Performing all of the following on a carrier class Internet Protocol (IP) network (e.g., national grade IP backbone):\n\n\n\n\na.Analysis at the application layer (e.g., Layer 7 of Open Systems Interconnection (OSI) model (ISO/IEC 7498-1));\n\n\nb.Extraction of selected metadata and application content (e.g., voice, video, messages, attachments); and\n\n\nc.Indexing of extracted data; and\n\n\n2.Being specially designed to carry out all of the following:\n\n\na.Execution of searches on the basis of 'hard selectors'; and\n\n\nb.Mapping of the relational network of an individual or of a group of people.\n\n\nNote:5A001.j. does not control systems or equipment, specially designed for any of the following:\n\n\na.Marketing purpose;\n\n\nb.Network Quality of Service (QoS); or\n\n\nc.Quality of Experience (QoE).\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Hard selectors' means data or set of data, related to an individual (e.g., family name, given name, e-mail, street address, phone number or group affiliations).\n\n\n5A101\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Telemetry and telecontrol equipment, including ground equipment, designed or modified for 'missiles'.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nIn 5A101 'missile' means complete rocket systems and unmanned aerial vehicle systems capable of a range exceeding 300 km.\n\n\nNote:5A101 does not control:\n\n\na.Equipment designed or modified for manned aircraft or satellites;\n\n\nb.Ground based equipment designed or modified for terrestrial or marine applications;\n\n\nc.Equipment designed for commercial, civil or 'Safety of Life' (e.g. data integrity, flight safety) GNSS services;\n\n\n5B1Test, Inspection and Production or\n\n\nNote:5B001.b.2.d. does not control equipment specially designed for the \"development\" of commercial TV systems.\n\n\n3.Not used;\n\n\n4.Radio equipment employing Quadrature-Amplitude-Modulation (QAM) techniques above level 256;\n\n\n5.Not used.\n\n\n5C1Materials\n\n\nNone\n\n\n5D1Software\n\n\n\n\n5D001\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Software\" as
