follows:\n\n\na.\"Technology\" according to the General Technology Note for the \"development\", \"production\" or \"use\" (excluding operation) of equipment, functions or features specified in 5A001 or \"software\" specified in 5D001.a.;\n\n\nb.Specific \"technology\" as follows:\n\n\n1.\"Required\" \"technology\" for the \"development\" or \"production\" of telecommunications equipment specially designed to be used on board satellites;\n\n\n2.\"Technology\" for the \"development\" or \"use\" of \"laser\" communication techniques with the capability of automatically acquiring and tracking signals and maintaining communications through exoatmosphere or sub-surface (water) media;\n\n\n3.\"Technology\" for the \"development\" of digital cellular radio base station receiving equipment whose reception capabilities that allow multi-band, multi-channel, multi-mode, multi-coding algorithm or multi-protocol operation can be modified by changes in \"software\";\n\n\n\n\n4.\"Technology\" for the \"development\" of \"spread spectrum\" techniques, including \"frequency hopping\" techniques;\n\n\nNote:5E001.b.4. does not control \"technology\" for the \"development\" of any of the following:\n\n\na.Civil cellular radio-communications systems; or\n\n\nb.Fixed or mobile satellite earth stations for commercial civil telecommunications.\n\n\nc.\"Technology\" according to the General Technology Note for the \"development\" or \"production\" of any of the following: \n\n\n1.Equipment employing digital techniques designed to operate at a \"total digital transfer rate\" exceeding 560 Gbit/s;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nFor telecommunication switching equipment the \"total digital transfer rate\" is the unidirectional speed of a single interface, measured at the highest speed port or line.\n\n\n2.Equipment employing a \"laser\" and having any of the following:\n\n\na.A transmission wavelength exceeding 1750 nm;\n\n\nb.Performing \"optical amplification\" using Praseodymium-Doped Fluoride Fibre Amplifiers (PDFFA);\n\n\nc.Employing coherent optical transmission or coherent optical detection techniques;\n\n\nNote:5E001.c.2.c. controls \"technology\" for the \"development\" or \"production\" of systems using an optical local oscillator in the receiving side to synchronize with a carrier \"laser\".\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nFor the purpose of 5E001.c.2.c., these techniques include optical heterodyne, homodyne or intradyne techniques.\n\n\nd.Employing wavelength division multiplexing techniques of optical carriers at less than 100 GHz spacing; or\n\n\ne.Employing analogue techniques and having a bandwidth exceeding 2,5 GHz;\n\n\nNote:5E001.c.2.e. does not control \"technology\" for the \"development\" or \"production\" of commercial TV systems.\n\n\nN.B.:For \"technology\" for the \"development\" or \"production\" of non-telecommunications equipment employing a laser, see 6E.\n\n\n3.Equipment employing \"optical switching\" and having a switching time less than 1 ms;\n\n\n\n\n4.Radio equipment having any of the following:\n\n\na.Quadrature-Amplitude-Modulation (QAM) techniques above level 256;\n\n\nb.Operating at input or output frequencies exceeding 31,8 GHz; or\n\n\nNote:5E001.c.4.b. does not control \"technology\" for the \"development\" or \"production\" of equipment designed or modified for operation in any frequency band which is \"allocated by the ITU\" for radio-communications services, but not for radio-determination.\n\n\nc.Operating in the 1,5 MHz to 87,5 MHz band and incorporating adaptive techniques providing more than 15 dB suppression of an interfering signal; or\n\n\n5.Not used;\n\n\n6.Mobile equipment having all of the following:\n\n\na.Operating at an optical wavelength greater than or equal to 200 nm and less than or equal to 400 nm; and\n\n\nb.Operating as a \"local area network\";\n\n\nd.\"Technology\" according to the General Technology Note for the \"development\" or \"production\" of Microwave Monolithic Integrated Circuit (MMIC) power amplifiers specially designed for telecommunications and that are any of the following:\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nFor purposes of 5E001.d., the parameter peak saturated power output may also be referred to on product data sheets as output power, saturated power output, maximum power output, peak power output, or peak envelope power output.\n\n\n1.Rated for operation at frequencies exceeding 2.7 GHz up to and including 6,8 GHz with a \"fractional bandwidth\" greater than 15 %, and having any of the following:\n\n\na.A peak saturated power output greater than 75 W (48,75 dBm) at any frequency exceeding 2,7 GHz up to and including 2,9 GHz;\n\n\nb.A peak saturated power output greater than 55 W (47,4 dBm) at any frequency exceeding 2,9 GHz up to and including 3,2 GHz;\n\n\nc.A peak saturated power output greater than 40 W (46 dBm) at any frequency exceeding 3,2 GHz up to and including 3,7 GHz; or\n\n\nd.A peak saturated power output greater than 20 W (43 dBm) at any frequency exceeding 3,7 GHz up to and including 6,8 GHz;\n\n\n2.Rated for operation at frequencies exceeding 6,8 GHz up to and including 16 GHz with a \"fractional bandwidth\" greater than 10 %, and having any of the following:\n\n\na.A peak saturated power output greater than 10 W (40 dBm) at any frequency exceeding 6,8 GHz up to and including 8,5 GHz; or\n\n\nb.A peak saturated power output greater than 5 W (37 dBm) at any frequency exceeding 8,5 GHz up to and including 16 GHz;\n\n\n\n\n3.Rated for operation with a peak saturated power output greater than 3 W (34,77 dBm) at any frequency exceeding 16 GHz up to and including 31,8 GHz, and with a \"fractional bandwidth\" of greater than 10 %;\n\n\n4.Rated for operation with a peak saturated power output greater than 0,1 nW (-70 dBm) at any frequency exceeding 31,8 GHz up to and including 37 GHz;\n\n\n5.Rated for operation with a peak saturated power output greater than 1 W (30 dBm) at any frequency exceeding 37 GHz up to and including 43,5 GHz, and with a \"fractional bandwidth\" of greater than 10 %;\n\n\n6.Rated for operation with a peak saturated power output greater than 31,62 mW (15 dBm) at any frequency exceeding 43,5 GHz up to and including 75 GHz, and with a \"fractional bandwidth\" of greater than 10 %;\n\n\n7.Rated for operation with a peak saturated power output greater than 10 mW (10 dBm) at any frequency exceeding 75 GHz up to and including 90 GHz, and with a \"fractional bandwidth\" of greater than 5 %; or\n\n\n8.Rated for operation with a peak saturated power output greater than 0,1 nW (-70 dBm) at any frequency exceeding 90 GHz;\n\n\ne.\"Technology\" according to the General Technology Note for the \"development\" or \"production\" of electronic devices and circuits, specially designed for telecommunications and containing components manufactured from \"superconductive\" materials, specially designed for operation at temperatures below the \"critical temperature\" of at least one of the \"superconductive\" constituents and having any of the following:\n\n\n1.Current switching for digital circuits using \"superconductive\" gates with a product of delay time per gate (in seconds) and power dissipation per gate (in watts) of less than 10\u201314 J; or\n\n\n2.Frequency selection at all frequencies using resonant circuits with Q-values exceeding 10000.\n\n\n5E101\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Technology\" according to the General Technology Note for the \"development\", \"production\" or \"use\" of equipment specified in 5A101.\n\n\nPART 2 \u2014\"INFORMATION SECURITY\"\n\n\nNote 1:The control status of \"information security\" items or functions is determined in Category 5, Part 2 even if they are components, \"software\" or functions of other systems or equipment.\n\n\nNote 2:Category 5 \u2013 Part 2 does not control products when accompanying their user for the user's personal use.\n\n\nNote 3:Cryptography Note 5A002 and 5D002 do not control items as follows:\n\n\na.Items that meet all of the following:\n\n\n1.Generally available to the public by being sold, without restriction, from stock at retail selling points by means of any of the following:\n\n\na.Over-the-counter transactions;\n\n\nb.Mail order transactions;\n\n\nc.Electronic transactions; or\n\n\nd.Telephone call transactions;\n\n\n\n\n2.The cryptographic functionality cannot easily be changed by the user;\n\n\n3.Designed for installation by the user without further substantial support by the supplier; and\n\n\n4.When necessary, details of the goods are accessible and will be provided, upon request, to the competent authorities of the Member State in which the exporter is established in order to ascertain compliance with conditions described in paragraphs 1. to 3. above;\n\n\nb.Hardware components or 'executable software', of existing items described in paragraph a. of this Note, that have been designed for these existing items, meeting all of the following:\n\n\n1.\"Information security\" is not the primary function or set of functions of the component or 'executable software';\n\n\n2.The component or 'executable software' does not change any cryptographic functionality of the existing items, or add new cryptographic functionality to the existing items;\n\n\n3.The feature set of the component or 'executable software' is fixed and is not designed or modified to customer specification; and\n\n\n4.When necessary as determined by the competent authorities of the Member State in which the exporter is established, details of the component or 'executable software' and details of relevant end-items are accessible and will be provided to the competent authority upon request, in order to ascertain compliance with conditions described above.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nFor the purpose of the Cryptography Note, 'executable software' means \"software\" in executable form, from an existing hardware component excluded from 5A002 by the Cryptography Note.\n\n\nNote:'Executable software' does not include complete binary images of the \"software\" running on an end-item.\n\n\nNote to the Cryptography Note:\n\n\n1.To meet paragraph a. of Note 3, all of the following must apply:\n\n\na.The item is of potential interest to a wide range of individuals and businesses; and\n\n\nb.The price and information about the main functionality of the item are available before purchase without the need to consult the vendor or supplier.\n\n\n2.In determining eligibility of paragraph a. of Note 3, competent authorities may take into account relevant factors such as quantity, price, required technical skill, existing sales channels, typical customers, typical use or any exclusionary practices of the supplier.\n\n\nNote 4:Category 5 \u2013 Part 2 does not control items incorporating or using \"cryptography\" and meeting all of the following:\n\n\na.The primary function or set of functions is not any of the following:\n\n\n1.\"Information security\";\n\n\n2.A computer, including operating systems, parts and components therefor;\n\n\n\n\n3.Sending, receiving or storing information (except in support of entertainment, mass commercial broadcasts, digital rights management or medical records management); or\n\n\n4.Networking (includes operation, administration, management and provisioning);\n\n\nb.The cryptographic functionality is limited to supporting their primary function or set of functions; and\n\n\nc.When necessary, details of the items are accessible and will be provided, upon request, to the competent authorities of the Member State in which the exporter is established in order to ascertain compliance with conditions described in paragraphs a. and b. above.\n\n\n5A2Systems, Equipment and Components\n\n\n5A002\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Information security\" systems, equipment and components therefor, as follows:\n\n\na.Systems, equipment and components for \"information security\", as follows,\n\n\nN.B.:For the control of Global Navigation Satellite Systems (GNSS) receiving equipment containing or employing decryption, see 7A005 and for related decryption \"software\" and \"technology\" see 7D005 and 7E001.\n\n\n1.Designed or modified to use \"cryptography\" employing digital techniques performing any cryptographic function other than authentication, digital signature or the execution of copy-protected \"software\", and having any of the following: \n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.Functions for authentication, digital signature and the execution of copy-protected \"software\" include their associated key management function.\n\n\n2.Authentication includes all aspects of access control where there is no encryption of files or text except as directly related to the protection of passwords, Personal Identification Numbers (PINs) or similar data to prevent unauthorised access.\n\n\na.A \"symmetric algorithm\" employing a key length in excess of 56 bits; or\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nIn Category 5 - Part 2, parity bits are not included in the key length.\n\n\nb.An \"asymmetric algorithm\" where the security of the algorithm is based on any of the following:\n\n\n1.Factorisation of integers in excess of 512 bits (e.g., RSA);\n\n\n2.Computation of discrete logarithms in a multiplicative group of a finite field of size greater than 512 bits (e.g., Diffie-Hellman over Z/pZ); or\n\n\n3.Discrete logarithms in a group other than mentioned in 5A002.a.1.b.2. in excess of 112 bits (e.g., Diffie-Hellman over an elliptic curve);\n\n\n2.Designed or modified to perform 'cryptanalytic functions';\n\n\n\n\nNote:5A002.a.2. includes systems or equipment, designed or modified to perform 'cryptanalytic functions' by means of reverse engineering.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Cryptanalytic functions' are functions designed to defeat cryptographic mechanisms in order to derive confidential variables or sensitive data, including clear text, passwords or cryptographic keys.\n\n\n3.Not used;\n\n\n4.Specially designed or modified to reduce the compromising emanations of information-bearing signals beyond what is necessary for health, safety or electromagnetic interference standards;\n\n\n5.Designed or modified to use cryptographic techniques to generate the spreading code for \"spread spectrum\" systems, other than those specified in 5A002.a.6., including the hopping code for \"frequency hopping\" systems;\n\n\n6.Designed or modified to use cryptographic techniques to generate channelising codes, scrambling codes or network identification codes, for systems using ultra-wideband modulation techniques and having any of the following:\n\n\na.A bandwidth exceeding 500 MHz; or\n\n\nb.A \"fractional bandwidth\" of 20 % or more;\n\n\n7.Non-cryptographic information and communications technology (ICT) security systems and devices that have been evaluated and certified by a national authority to exceed class EAL-6 (evaluation assurance level) of the Common Criteria (CC) or equivalent;\n\n\n8.Communications cable systems designed or modified using mechanical, electrical or electronic means to detect surreptitious intrusion;\n\n\nNote:5A002.a.8. only controls physical layer security.\n\n\n9.Designed or modified to use or perform \"quantum cryptography\".\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n\"Quantum cryptography\" is also known as Quantum Key Distribution (QKD).\n\n\nb.Systems, equipment, and components, designed or modified to enable, by means of \"cryptographic activation\" an item to achieve or exceed the controlled performance levels for functionality specified by 5A002.a. that would not otherwise be enabled.\n\n\nNote:5A002 does not control any of the following:\n\n\na.Smart cards and smart card 'readers/writers' as follows:\n\n\n1.A smart card or an electronically readable personal document (e.g., token coin, e-passport) that meets any of the following:\n\n\na.The cryptographic capability is restricted for use in equipment or systems excluded from 5A002 by Note 4 in Category 5 \u2013 Part 2 or entries b. to i. of this Note, and cannot be reprogrammed for any other use; or\n\n\n\n\nb.Having all of the following:\n\n\n1.It is specially designed and limited to allow protection of 'personal data' stored within;\n\n\n2.Has been, or can only be, personalized for public or commercial transactions or individual identification; and\n\n\n3.Where the cryptographic capability is not user-accessible;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Personal data' includes any data specific to a particular person or entity, such as the amount of money stored and data necessary for authentication.\n\n\n2.'Readers/writers' specially designed or modified, and limited, for items specified by a.1. of this Note.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Readers/writers' include equipment that communicates with smart cards or electronically readable documents through a network.\n\n\nb.Not used;\n\n\nc.Not used;\n\n\nd.Cryptographic equipment specially designed and limited for banking use or 'money transactions';\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Money transactions' in 5A002 Note d. includes the collection and settlement of fares or credit functions.\n\n\ne.Portable or mobile radiotelephones for civil use (e.g., for use with commercial civil cellular radio communication systems) that are not capable of transmitting encrypted data directly to another radiotelephone or equipment (other than Radio Access Network (RAN) equipment), nor of passing encrypted data through RAN equipment (e.g., Radio Network Controller (RNC) or Base Station Controller (BSC));\n\n\nf.Cordless telephone equipment not capable of end-to-end encryption where the maximum effective range of unboosted cordless operation (i.e. a single, unrelayed hop between terminal and home base station) is less than 400 metres according to the manufacturer's specifications;\n\n\ng.Portable or mobile radiotelephones and similar client wireless devices for civil use, that implement only published or commercial cryptographic standards (except for anti-piracy functions, which may be non-published) and also meet the provisions of paragraphs a.2. to a.4. of the Cryptography Note (Note 3 in Category 5, Part 2), that have been customised for a specific civil industry application with features that do not affect the cryptographic functionality of these original non-customised devices;\n\n\nh.Not used;\n\n\ni.Wireless \"personal area network\" equipment that implement only published or commercial cryptographic standards and where the cryptographic capability is limited to a nominal operating range not exceeding 30 metres according to the manufacturer's specifications, or not exceeding 100 metres according to the manufacturer's specifications for equipment that cannot interconnect with more than seven devices;\n\n\nj.Equipment, having no functionality specified by 5A002.a.2., 5A002.a.4., 5A002.a.7.,5A002.a.8 or 5A002.b. meeting all of the following:\n\n\n\n\n1.All cryptographic capability specified by 5A002.a. meets any of the following:\n\n\na.It cannot be used; or\n\n\nb.It can only be made useable by means of \"cryptographic activation\", and\n\n\n2.When necessary as determined by the competent authorities of the Member State in which the exporter is established, details of the equipment are accessible and will be provided to the authority upon request, in order to ascertain compliance with conditions described above;\n\n\nN.B. 1:See 5A002.a. for equipment that has undergone \"cryptographic activation\".\n\n\nN.B. 2:See also 5A002.b., 5D002.d. and 5E002.b.\n\n\nk.Mobile telecommunications Radio Access Network (RAN) equipment designed for civil use, which also meet the provisions of paragraphs a.2. to a.4. of the Cryptography Note (Note 3 in Category 5, Part 2), having an RF output power limited to 0,1 W (20 dBm) or less, and supporting 16 or fewer concurrent users.\n\n\nl.Routers, switches or relays, where the \"information security\" functionality is limited to the tasks of \"Operations, Administration or Maintenance\" (\"OAM\") implementing only published or commercial cryptographic standards; or\n\n\nm.General purpose computing equipment or servers, where the \"information security\" functionality meets all of the following:\n\n\n1.Uses only published or commercial cryptographic standards; and\n\n\n2.Is any of the following:\n\n\na.Integral to a CPU that meets the provisions of Note 3 to Category 5\u2013Part 2;\n\n\nb.Integral to an operating system that is not specified by 5D002.; or\n\n\nc.Limited to \"OAM\" of the equipment.\n\n\n5B2Test, Inspection and Production Equipment\n\n\n5B002\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Information security\" test, inspection and \"production\" equipment, as follows:\n\n\na.Equipment follows:\n\n\n\n\n1.Active (transmitting or transmitting-and-receiving) systems, equipment and specially designed components therefor, as follows:\n\n\nNote:6A001.a.1. does not control equipment as follows:\n\n\na.Depth sounders operating vertically below the apparatus, not including a scanning function exceeding \u00b1 20\u00b0, and limited to measuring the depth of water, the distance of submerged or buried objects or fish finding;\n\n\nb.Acoustic beacons, as follows:\n\n\n1.Acoustic emergency beacons;\n\n\n2.Pingers specially designed for relocating or returning to an underwater position.\n\n\na.Acoustic seabed survey equipment as follows:\n\n\n1.Surface vessel survey equipment designed for seabed topographic mapping and having all of the following:\n\n\na.Designed to take measurements at an angle exceeding 20\u00b0 from the vertical;\n\n\nb.Designed to measure seabed topography at seabed depths exceeding 600 m;\n\n\nc.'Sounding resolution' less than 2; and\n\n\nd.'Enhancement' of the depth accuracy through compensation for all the following:\n\n\n1.Motion of the acoustic sensor;\n\n\n2.In-water propagation from sensor to the seabed and back;\n\n\n3.Sound speed at the sensor;\n\n\nTechnical Notes\n\n\n1.Sounding resolution' is the swath width (degrees) divided by the maximum number of soundings per swath.\n\n\n2.'Enhancement' includes the ability to compensate by external means.\n\n\n2.Underwater survey equipment designed for seabed topographic mapping and having any of the following:\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n\n\nThe acoustic sensor pressure rating determines the depth rating of the equipment specified in 6A001.a.1.a.2.\n\n\na.Having all of the following:\n\n\n1.Designed or modified to operate at depths exceeding 300 m; and\n\n\n2.'Sounding rate' greater than 3,800 m/s; or\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Sounding rate' is the product of the maximum speed (m/s) at which the sensor can operate and the maximum number of soundings per swath assuming 100 % coverage. For systems that produce soundings in two directions (3D sonars), the maximum of the 'sounding rate' in either direction should be used\n\n\nb.Survey equipment, not specified in 6A001.a.1.a.2.a., having all of the following:\n\n\n1.Designed or modified to operate at depths exceeding 100 m;\n\n\n2.Designed to take measurements at an angle exceeding 20\u00b0 from the vertical;\n\n\n3.Having any of the following:\n\n\na.Operating frequency below 350 kHz; or\n\n\nb.Designed to measure seabed topography at a range exceeding 200 m from the acoustic sensor; and\n\n\n4.'Enhancement' of the depth accuracy through compensation of all of the following:\n\n\na.Motion of the acoustic sensor;\n\n\nb.In-water propagation from sensor to the seabed and back; and\n\n\nc.Sound speed at the sensor;\n\n\n3.Side Scan Sonar (SSS) or Synthetic Aperture Sonar (SAS), designed for seabed imaging and having all of the following, and specially designed transmitting and receiving acoustic arrays therefor:\n\n\na.Designed or modified to operate at depths exceeding 500 m;\n\n\nb.An 'area coverage rate' of greater than 570 m2/s while operating at the maximum range that it can operate with an 'along track resolution' of less than 15 cm; and\n\n\nc.An 'across track resolution' of less than 15 cm;\n\n\n\n\nTechnical Notes\n\n\n1.'Area coverage rate' (m2/s) is twice the product of the sonar range (m) and the maximum speed (m/s) at which the sensor can operate at that range.\n\n\n2.'Along track resolution' (cm), for SSS only, is the product of azimuth (horizontal) beamwidth (degrees) and sonar range (m) and 0,873.\n\n\n3.'Across track resolution' (cm) is 75 divided by the signal bandwidth (kHz).\n\n\nb.Systems or transmitting and receiving arrays, designed for object detection or location, having any of the following:\n\n\n1.A transmitting frequency below 10 kHz;\n\n\n2.Sound pressure level exceeding 224 dB (reference 1 \u03bcPa at 1 m) for equipment with an operating frequency in the band from 10 kHz to 24 kHz inclusive;\n\n\n3.Sound pressure level exceeding 235 dB (reference 1 \u03bcPa at 1 m) for equipment with an operating frequency in the band between 24 kHz and 30 kHz;\n\n\n4.Forming beams of less than 1\u00b0 on any axis and having an operating frequency of less than 100 kHz;\n\n\n5.Designed to operate with an unambiguous display range exceeding 5,120 m; or\n\n\n6.Designed to withstand pressure during normal operation at depths exceeding 1000 m and having transducers with any of the following:\n\n\na.Dynamic compensation for pressure; or\n\n\nb.Incorporating other than lead zirconate titanate as the transduction element;\n\n\nc.Acoustic projectors, including transducers, incorporating piezoelectric, magnetostrictive, electrostrictive, electrodynamic or hydraulic elements operating individually or in a designed combination and having any of the following:\n\n\nNote 1:The control status of acoustic projectors, including transducers, specially designed for other equipment not specified in 6A001 is determined by the control status of the other equipment.\n\n\nNote 2:6A001.a.1.c. does not control electronic sources which direct the sound vertically only, or mechanical (e.g., air gun or vapour-shock gun) or chemical (e.g., explosive) sources.\n\n\nNote 3:Piezoelectric elements specified in 6A001.a.1.c. include those made from lead-magnesium-niobate/lead-titanate (Pb(Mg1/3Nb2/3)O3-PbTiO3, or PMN-PT) single crystals grown from solid solution or lead-indium-niobate/lead-magnesium niobate/lead-titanate (Pb(In1/2Nb1/2)O3\u2013Pb(Mg1/3Nb2/3)O3\u2013PbTiO3, or PIN-PMN-PT) single crystals grown from solid solution.\n\n\n1.Operating at frequencies below 10 kHz and having any of the following:\n\n\na.Not designed for continuous operation at 100 % duty cycle and having a radiated 'free-field Source Level (SLRMS)' exceeding (10log(f) + 169,77) dB (reference 1 \u03bcPa at 1 m) where f is the frequency in Hertz of maximum Transmitting Voltage Response (TVR) below 10 kHz; or\n\n\nb.Designed for continuous operation at 100 % duty cycle and having a continuously radiated 'free-field Source Level (SLRMS)' at 100 % duty cycle exceeding (10log(f) + 159,77) dB (reference 1 \u03bcPa at 1 m) where f is the frequency in Hertz of maximum Transmitting Voltage Response (TVR) below 10 kHz; or\n\n\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nThe 'free-field Source Level ( SLRMS' is defined along the maximum response axis and in the far field of the acoustic projector. It can be obtained from the Transmitting Voltage Response using the following equation: SLRMS = (TVR + 20log VRMS) dB (ref 1\u03bcPa at 1 m), where SLRMS is the source level, TVR is the Transmitting Voltage Response and VRMS is the Driving Voltage of the Projector.\n\n\n2.Not used\n\n\n3.Side-lobe suppression exceeding 22 dB;\n\n\nd.Acoustic systems and equipment, designed to determine the position of surface vessels or underwater vehicles and having all the following, and specially designed components therefor:\n\n\n1.Detection range exceeding 1000 m; and\n\n\n2.Positioning accuracy of less than 10 m rms (root mean square) when measured at a range of 1000 m;\n\n\nNote:6A001.a.1.d. includes:\n\n\na.Equipment using coherent \"signal processing\" between two or more beacons and the hydrophone unit carried by the surface vessel or underwater vehicle;\n\n\nb.Equipment capable of automatically correcting speed-of-sound propagation errors for calculation of a point.\n\n\ne.Active individual sonars, specially designed or modified to detect, locate and automatically classify swimmers or divers, having all of the following, and specially designed transmitting and receiving acoustic arrays therefor:\n\n\n1.Detection range exceeding 530 m;\n\n\n2.Positioning accuracy of less than 15 m rms (root mean square) when measured at a ran\u0121e of 530 m; and\n\n\n3.Transmitted pulse signal bandwidth exceeding 3 kHz;\n\n\nN.B:.For diver detection systems specially designed or modified for military use, see the Military Goods Controls.\n\n\nNote:For 6A001.a.1.e., where multiple detection ranges are specified for various environments, the greatest detection range is used.\n\n\n\n\u00ea 2420/2015 Art. 1.1 and Annex I\n\n\n\u00e81 2420/2015 Art. 1.1 and Annex I amended by Corrigendum, OJ L 060, 5.3.2016, p. 93\n\n\n2.Passive systems, equipment and specially designed components therefor, as follows:\n\n\n\n\na.Hydrophones having any of the following:\n\n\nNote:The control status of hydrophones specially designed for other equipment is determined by the control status of the other equipment.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nHydrophones consist of one or more sensing elements producing a single acoustic output channel. Those that contain multiple elements can be referred to as a hydrophone group.\n\n\n1.Incorporating continuous flexible sensing elements;\n\n\n2.Incorporating flexible assemblies of discrete sensing elements with either a diameter or length less than 20 mm and with a separation between elements of less than 20 mm;\n\n\n3.Having any of the following sensing elements:\n\n\na.Optical fibres;\n\n\nb.'Piezoelectric polymer films' other than polyvinylidene-fluoride (PVDF) and its co-polymers {}{P(VDF-TrFE) and P(VDF-TFE)}};\n\n\nc.'Flexible piezoelectric composites';\n\n\nd.Lead-magnesium-niobate/lead-titanate (i.e., Pb(Mg1/3Nb2/3)O3-PbTiO3, or PMN-PT) piezoelectric single crystals grown from solid solution; or\n\n\ne.Lead-indium-niobate/lead-magnesium niobate/lead-titanate (i.e., Pb(In1/2Nb1/2)O3\u2013Pb(Mg1/3Nb2/3)O3\u2013PbTiO3, or PIN-PMN-PT) piezoelectric single crystals grown from solid solution;\n\n\n4.A 'hydrophone sensitivity' better than \u2013 180 dB at any depth with no acceleration compensation;\n\n\n5.Designed to operate at depths exceeding 35 m with acceleration compensation; or\n\n\n6.Designed for operation at depths exceeding 1000 m;\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.'Piezoelectric polymer film' sensing elements consist of polarised polymer film that is stretched over and attached to a supporting frame or spool (mandrel).\n\n\n2.'Flexible piezoelectric composite' sensing elements consist of piezoelectric ceramic particles or fibres combined with an electrically insulating, acoustically transparent rubber, polymer or epoxy compound, where the compound is an integral part of the sensing elements.\n\n\n3.'Hydrophone sensitivity' is defined as twenty times the logarithm to the base 10 of the ratio of rms output voltage to a 1 V rms reference, when the hydrophone sensor, without a pre-amplifier, is placed in a plane wave acoustic field with an rms pressure of 1 \u03bcPa. For example, a hydrophone of \u2013 160 dB (reference 1 V per \u03bcPa) would yield an output voltage of 10\u20138 V in such a field, while one of \u2013 180 dB sensitivity would yield only 10\u20139 V output. Thus, \u2013 160 dB is better than \u2013 180 dB.\n\n\nb.Towed acoustic hydrophone arrays having any of the following:\n\n\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nHydrophone arrays consist of a number of hydrophones providing multiple acoustic output channels.\n\n\n1.Hydrophone group spacing of less than 12,5 m or 'able to be modified' to have hydrophone group spacing of less than 12,5 m;\n\n\n2.Designed or 'able to be modified' to operate at depths exceeding 35 m;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Able to be modified' in 6A001.a.2.b.1. and 2. means having provisions to allow a change of the wiring or interconnections to alter hydrophone group spacing or operating depth limits. These provisions are: spare wiring exceeding 10 % of the number of wires, hydrophone group spacing adjustment blocks or internal depth limiting devices that are adjustable or that control more than one hydrophone group.\n\n\n3.Heading sensors specified in 6A001.a.2.d.;\n\n\n4.Longitudinally reinforced array hoses;\n\n\n5.An assembled array of less than 40 mm in diameter;\n\n\n6.Not used;\n\n\n7.Hydrophone characteristics specified in 6A001.a.2.a.; or\n\n\n8.Accelerometer-based hydro-acoustic sensors specified in 6A001.a.2.g.;\n\n\nc.Processing equipment, specially designed for towed acoustic hydrophone arrays, having \"user accessible programmability\" and time or frequency domain processing and correlation, including spectral analysis, digital filtering and beamforming using Fast Fourier or other transforms or processes;\n\n\nd.Heading sensors having all of the following:\n\n\n1.An accuracy of better than \u00b1 0,5 \u00b0; and\n\n\n2.Designed to operate at depths exceeding 35 m or having an adjustable or removable depth sensing device in order to operate at depths exceeding 35 m;\n\n\ne.Bottom or bay-cable hydrophone arrays, having any of the following:\n\n\n1.Incorporating hydrophones specified in 6A001.a.2.a.;\n\n\n2.Incorporating multiplexed hydrophone group signal modules having all of the following characteristics:\n\n\na.Designed to operate at depths exceeding 35 m or having an adjustable or removable depth sensing device in order to operate at depths exceeding 35 m; and\n\n\n\n\nb.Capable of being operationally interchanged with towed acoustic hydrophone array modules; o\n\n\n3.Incorporating accelerometer-based hydro-acoustic sensors specified in 6A001.a.2.g.;\n\n\nf.Processing equipment, specially designed for bottom or bay cable systems, having \"user accessible programmability\" and time or frequency domain processing and correlation, including spectral analysis, digital filtering and beamforming using Fast Fourier or other transforms or processes;\n\n\ng.Accelerometer-based hydro-acoustic sensors having all of the following:\n\n\n1.Composed of three accelerometers arranged along three distinct axes;\n\n\n2.Having an overall 'acceleration sensitivity' better than 48 dB (reference 1,000 mV rms per 1 g);\n\n\n3.Designed to operate at depths greater than 35 meters; and\n\n\n4.Operating frequency below 20 kHz.\n\n\nNote:6A001.a.2.g. does not control particle velocity sensors or geophones.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.Accelerometer-based hydro-acoustic sensors are also known as vector sensors.\n\n\n2.'Acceleration sensitivity' is defined as twenty times the logarithm to the base 10 of the ratio of rms output voltage to a 1 V rms reference, when the hydro-acoustic sensor, without a preamplifier, is placed in a plane wave acoustic field with an rms acceleration of 1 g (i.e., 9,81 m/s2).\n\n\nNote:6A001.a.2. also controls receiving equipment, whether or not related in normal application to separate active equipment, and specially designed components therefor.\n\n\nb.Correlation-velocity and Doppler-velocity sonar log equipment, designed to measure the horizontal speed of the equipment carrier relative to the sea bed, as follows:\n\n\n1.Correlation-velocity sonar log equipment having any of the following characteristics:\n\n\na.Designed to operate at distances between the carrier and the sea bed exceeding 500 m; or\n\n\nb.Having speed accuracy better than 1 % of speed;\n\n\n2.Doppler-velocity sonar log equipment having speed accuracy better than 1 % of speed.\n\n\nNote 1:6A001.b. does not control depth sounders limited to any of the following:\n\n\na.Measuring the depth of water;\n\n\n\n\nb.Measuring the distance of submerged or buried objects; or\n\n\nc.Fish finding.\n\n\nNote 2:6A001.b. does not control equipment specially designed for installation on surface vessels.\n\n\nc.Not used.\n\n\n6A002\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Optical sensors or equipment and components therefor, as follows:\n\n\nN.B.:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0SEE ALSO 6A102.\n\n\na.Optical detectors as follows:\n\n\n1.\"Space-qualified\" solid-state detectors as follows:\n\n\nNote:For the purpose of 6A002.a.1., solid-state detectors include \"focal plane arrays\".\n\n\na.\"Space-qualified\" solid-state detectors having all of the following:\n\n\n1.A peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 10 nm but not exceeding 300 nm; and\n\n\n2.A response of less than 0,1 % relative to the peak response at a wavelength exceeding 400 nm;\n\n\nb.\"Space-qualified\" solid-state detectors having all of the following:\n\n\n1.A peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 900 nm but not exceeding 1200 nm; and\n\n\n2.A response \"time constant\" of 95 ns or less;\n\n\nc.\"Space-qualified\" solid-state detectors having a peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 1200 nm but not exceeding 30000 nm;\n\n\nd.\"Space-qualified\" \"focal plane arrays\" having more than 2048 elements per array and having a peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 300 nm but not exceeding 900 nm\n\n\n2.Image intensifier tubes and specially designed components therefor, as follows:\n\n\nNote:6A002.a.2. does not control non-imaging photomultiplier tubes having an electron sensing device in the vacuum space limited solely to any of the following:\n\n\na.A single metal anode; or\n\n\n\n\nb.Metal anodes with a centre to centre spacing greater than 500 \u03bcm.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Charge multiplication' is a form of electronic image amplification and is defined as the generation of charge carriers as a result of an impact ionization gain process. 'Charge multiplication' sensors may take the form of an image intensifier tube, solid state detector or \"focal plane array\".\n\n\na.Image intensifier tubes having all of the following:\n\n\n1.A peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 400 nm but not exceeding 1050 nm;\n\n\n2.Electron image amplification using any of the following:\n\n\na.\u00e81 A microchannel plate with a hole pitch (centre-to-centre spacing) of 12 \u03bcm or less; or \u00e7\n\n\nb.An electron sensing device with a non-binned pixel pitch of 500 \u03bcm or less, specially designed or modified to achieve 'charge multiplication' other than by a microchannel plate; and\n\n\n3.Any of the following photocathodes: \n\n\na.Multialkali photocathodes (e.g., S-20 and S-25) having a luminous sensitivity exceeding 350 \u03bcA/lm;\n\n\nb.GaAs or GaInAs photocathodes; or\n\n\nc.Other \"III/V compound\" semiconductor photocathodes having a maximum \"radiant sensitivity\" exceeding 10 mA/W;\n\n\nb.Image intensifier tubes having all of the following:\n\n\n1.A peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 1050 nm but not exceeding 1800 nm;\n\n\n2.Electron image amplification using any of the following:\n\n\na.A microchannel plate with a hole pitch (centre-to-centre spacing) of 12 \u03bcm or less; or\n\n\nb.An electron sensing device with a non-binned pixel pitch of 500 \u03bcm or less, specially designed or modified to achieve 'charge multiplication' other than by a microchannel plate; and\n\n\n3.\"III/V compound\" semiconductor (e.g., GaAs or GaInAs) photocathodes and transferred electron photocathodes, having a maximum \"radiant sensitivity\" exceeding 15 mA/W;\n\n\nc.Specially designed components as follows:\n\n\n1.Microchannel plates having a hole pitch (centre-to-centre spacing) of 12 \u03bcm or less;\n\n\n\n\n2.An electron sensing device with a non-binned pixel pitch of 500 \u03bcm or less, specially designed or modified to achieve 'charge multiplication' other than by a microchannel plate;\n\n\n3.\"III/V compound\" semiconductor (e.g., GaAs or GaInAs) photocathodes and transferred electron photocathodes;\n\n\nNote:6A002.a.2.c.3. does not control compound semiconductor photocathodes designed to achieve a maximum \"radiant sensitivity\" of any of the following:\n\n\na.10 mA/W or less at the peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 400 nm but not exceeding 1 050 nm; or\n\n\nb.15 mA/W or less at the peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 1050 nm but not exceeding 1800 nm.\n\n\n3.Non-\"space-qualified\" \"focal plane arrays\" as follows:\n\n\nN.B.:'Microbolometer' non-\"space-qualified\" \"focal plane arrays\" are only specified in 6A002.a.3.f.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nLinear or two-dimensional multi-element detector arrays are referred to as \"focal plane arrays\";\n\n\nNote 1:6A002.a.3. includes photoconductive arrays and photovoltaic arrays.\n\n\nNote 2:6A002.a.3. does not control:\n\n\na.Multi-element (not to exceed 16 elements) encapsulated photoconductive cells using either lead sulphide or lead selenide;\n\n\nb.Pyroelectric detectors using any of the following:\n\n\n1.Triglycine sulphate and variants;\n\n\n2.Lead-lanthanum-zirconium titanate and variants;\n\n\n3.Lithium tantalate;\n\n\n4.Polyvinylidene fluoride and variants; or\n\n\n5.Strontium barium niobate and variants;\n\n\nc.\"Focal plane arrays\" specially designed or modified to achieve 'charge multiplication' and limited by design to have a maximum \"radiant sensitivity\" of 10 mA/W or less for wavelengths exceeding 760 nm, having all of the following:\n\n\n1.Incorporating a response limiting mechanism designed not to be removed or modified; and\n\n\n\n\n2.Any of the following:\n\n\na.The response limiting mechanism is integral to or combined with the detector element; or\n\n\nb.The \"focal plane array\" is only operable with the response limiting mechanism in place.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nA response limiting mechanism integral to the detector element is designed not to be removed or modified without rendering the detector inoperable.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Charge multiplication' is a form of electronic image amplification and is defined as the generation of charge carriers as a result of an impact ionization gain process. 'Charge multiplication' sensors may take the form of an image intensifier tube, solid state detector or \"focal plane array\".\n\n\na.Non-\"space-qualified\" \"focal plane arrays\" having all of the following: \n\n\n1.Individual elements with a peak response within the wavelength range exceeding 900 nm but not exceeding 1050 nm; and\n\n\n2.Any of the following:\n\n\na.A response \"time constant\" of less than 0,5 ns; or\n\n\nb.Specially designed or modified to achieve 'charge multiplication' and having a maximum \"radiant sensitivity\" exceeding 10 mA/W;\n\n\nb.Non-\"space-qualified\" \"focal plane arrays\" having all of the following:\n\n\n1.Individual elements with a peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 1050 nm but not exceeding 1200 nm; and\n\n\n2.Any of the mA/W;\n\n\nc.Non-\"space-qualified\" non-linear (2-dimensional) \"focal plane arrays\" having individual elements with a peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 1200 nm but not exceeding 30000 nm;\n\n\nN.B.:Silicon and other material based 'microbolometer' non-\"space-qualified\" \"focal plane arrays\" are only specified in 6A002.a.3.f.\n\n\nd.Non-\"space-qualified\" linear (1-dimensional) \"focal plane arrays\" having all of the following:\n\n\n\n\n1.Individual elements with a peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 1200 nm but not exceeding 3000 nm; and\n\n\n2.Any of the detector elements;\n\n\nNote:6A002.a.3.d. does not control \"focal plane arrays\" (not to exceed 32 elements) having detector elements limited solely to germanium material.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nFor the purposes of 6A002.a.3.d., 'cross-scan direction' is defined as the axis parallel to the linear array of detector elements and the 'scan direction' is defined as the axis perpendicular to the linear array of detector elements.\n\n\ne.Non-\"space-qualified\" linear (1-dimensional) \"focal plane arrays\" having individual elements with a peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 3000 nm but not exceeding 30000 nm;\n\n\nf.Non-\"space-qualified\" non-linear (2-dimensional) infrared \"focal plane arrays\" based on 'microbolometer' material having individual elements with an unfiltered response in the wavelength range equal to or exceeding 8000 nm but not exceeding 14000 nm;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nFor the purposes of 6A002.a.3.f., 'microbolometer' is defined as a thermal imaging detector that, as a result of a temperature change in the detector caused by the absorption of infrared radiation, is used to generate any usable signal.\n\n\ng.Non-\"space-qualified\" \"focal plane arrays\" having all of the following:\n\n\n1.Individual detector elements with a peak response in the wavelength range exceeding 400 nm but not exceeding 900 nm;\n\n\n2.Specially designed or modified to achieve 'charge multiplication' and having a maximum \"radiant sensitivity\" exceeding 10 mA/W for wavelengths exceeding 760 nm; and\n\n\n3.Greater than 32 elements;\n\n\nb.\"Monospectral imaging sensors\" and \"multispectral imaging sensors\", designed for remote sensing applications and having any of the following:\n\n\n1.An Instantaneous-Field-Of-View (IFOV) of less than 200 \u03bcrad (microradians); or\n\n\n2.Specified for operation in the wavelength range exceeding 400 nm but not exceeding 30000 nm and having all the following;\n\n\na.Providing output imaging data in digital format; and\n\n\nb.Having any of the following characteristics:\n\n\n\n\n1.\"Space-qualified\"; or\n\n\n2.Designed for airborne operation, using other than silicon detectors, and having an IFOV of less than 2,5 mrad (milliradians);\n\n\nNote:6A002.b.1. does not control \"monospectral imaging sensors\" with a peak response in the achieve 'charge multiplication'.\n\n\nc.'Direct view' imaging equipment incorporating any of the following:\n\n\n1.Image intensifier tubes specified in 6A002.a.2.a. or 6A002.a.2.b.;\n\n\n2.\"Focal plane arrays\" specified in 6A002.a.3.; or\n\n\n3.Solid state detectors specified in 6A002.a.1.;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Direct view' refers to imaging equipment that presents a visual image to a human observer without converting the image into an electronic signal for television display, and that cannot record or store the image photographically, electronically or by any other means.\n\n\nNote:6A002.c. does not control equipment as follows, when incorporating other than GaAs or GaInAs photocathodes:\n\n\na.Industrial or civilian intrusion alarm, traffic or industrial Note 3.b. refers to an imaging camera operating in the infrared spectrum that presents a visual image to a human observer using a near-to-eye micro display incorporating any light-security mechanism.\n\n\nNote 4:6A003.b.4.c. does not control imaging cameras having any of the following:\n\n\na.Having all of the following:\n\n\n1.Where the camera is specially designed for installation as manufactured with the intent to meet, or exceed, the control parameter.\n\n\nNote6A004.e. does not control 'aspheric optical elements' having any of the following:\n\n\na.Largest optical-aperture expansion greater than 2,5 \u00d7 10\u20136 /K at 25 \u00b0C; or\n\n\ne.An x-ray optical element having inner mirror capabilities (e.g., tube-type mirrors).\n\n\nN.B.For 'aspheric optical elements' specially designed for lithography equipment, see 3B001.\n\n\n6A005\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Lasers\", other than those specified in 0B001.g.5. or 0B001.h.6., components and optical equipment, as follows:\n\n\nN.B.:SEE ALSO 6A205.\n\n\nNote 1:Pulsed \"lasers\" include those that run in a continuous wave (CW) mode with pulses superimposed.\n\n\nNote 2:Excimer, semiconductor, chemical, CO, CO2, and 'non-repetitive pulsed' Nd:glass \"lasers\" are only specified in 6A005.d.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Non-repetitive pulsed' refers to \"lasers\" that produce either a single output pulse or that have a time interval between pulses exceeding one minute.\n\n\nNote 3:6A005 includes fibre \"lasers\".\n\n\nNote 4:The control status of \"lasers\" incorporating frequency conversion (i.e., wavelength change) by means other than one \"laser\" pumping another \"laser\" is determined by applying the control parameters for both the output of the source \"laser\" and the frequency-converted optical output.\n\n\nNote 5:6A005 does not control \"lasers\" as follows:\n\n\na.Ruby with output energy below 20 J;\n\n\nb.Nitrogen;\n\n\nc.Krypton.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nIn 6A005 'Wall-plug efficiency' is defined as the ratio of \"laser\" output power (or \"average output power\") to total electrical input power required to operate the \"laser\", including the power supply/conditioning and thermal conditioning/heat exchanger.\n\n\na.Non-\"tunable\" continuous wave \"(CW) lasers\" having any of the following:\n\n\n1.Output wavelength less than 150 nm and output power exceeding 1 W;\n\n\n\n\n2.Output wavelength of 150 nm or more but not exceeding 510 nm and output power exceeding 30 W;\n\n\nNote:6A005.a.2. does not control Argon \"lasers\" having an output power equal to or and\n\n\n4.Permanently installed;\n\n\n\n\nc.Weather balloon tracking radars.\n\n\nj.Being \"laser\" radar or Light Detection and Ranging (LIDAR) equipment and having any of the following: \n\n\n1.\"Space-qualified\";\n\n\n2.Employing coherent heterodyne or homodyne detection techniques and having an angular resolution of less (better) than 20 \u03bcrad (microradians); or\n\n\n3.Designed for carrying out airborne bathymetric littoral surveys to International Hydrographic Organization (IHO) Order 1a Standard (5th Edition February 2008) for Hydrographic Surveys or better, and using one or more lasers with a wavelength exceeding 400 nm but not exceeding 600 nm;\n\n\nNote 1:LIDAR equipment specially designed for surveying is only specified in 6A008.j.3.\n\n\nNote 2:6A008.j. does not control LIDAR equipment specially designed for meteorological observation.\n\n\nNote 3:Parameters in the IHO Order 1a Standard 5th Edition February 2008 are summarized as follows:\n\n\n\u2013Horizontal Accuracy (95 % Confidence Level) = 5 m + 5 % of depth.\n\n\n\u2013Depth Accuracy for Reduced Depths (95 % confidence level) =\u00b1\u221aa2+(b*d)2), where:\n\n\n\n\n\na\n\n\n\n\n=\n\n\n\n\n0,5 m = constant depth error, i.e. the sum of all constant depth errors\n\n\n\n\n\n\nb\n\n\n\n\n=\n\n\n\n\n0,013 = factor of depth dependent error\n\n\n\n\n\n\nb*d\n\n\n\n\n=\n\n\n\n\ndepth dependent error, i.e. the sum of all depth dependent errors\n\n\n\n\n\n\nd\n\n\n\n\n=\n\n\n\n\ndepth\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\u2013Feature Detection = Cubic features > 2 m in depths up to 40 m;10 % of depth beyond 40 m.\n\n\nk.Having \"signal processing\" sub-systems using \"pulse compression\" and having any of the following:\n\n\n1.A \"pulse compression\" ratio exceeding 150; or\n\n\n2.A compressed pulse width of less than 200 ns; or\n\n\nNote:6A008.k.2. does not control two dimensional 'marine radar' or 'vessel traffic service' radar, having all of the following;\n\n\na.\"Pulse compression\" ratio not exceeding 150;\n\n\nb.Compressed pulse width of greater than 30 ns;\n\n\nc.Single and rotating mechanically scanned antenna;\n\n\n\n\nd.Peak output power not exceeding 250 W; and\n\n\ne.Not capable of \"frequency hopping\".\n\n\nl.Having data processing sub-systems and having any of the following:\n\n\n1.\"Automatic target tracking\" providing, at any antenna rotation, the predicted target position beyond the time of the next antenna beam passage; or\n\n\nNote:6A008.l.1. does not control conflict alert capability in ATC systems, or 'marine radar'.\n\n\n2.Not used;\n\n\n3.Not used;\n\n\n4.Configured to provide superposition and correlation, or fusion, of target data within six seconds from two or more \"geographically dispersed\" radar sensors to improve the aggregate performance beyond that of any single sensor specified by 6A008.f. or 6A008.i.\n\n\nN.B.See also Military Goods Controls.\n\n\nNote:6A008.l.4. does not control systems, equipment and assemblies used for 'vessel traffic service'.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.For the purposes of 6A008, 'marine radar' is a radar that is used to navigate safely at sea, inland waterways or near-shore environments.\n\n\n2.For the purposes of 6A008, 'vessel traffic service' is a vessel traffic monitoring and control service similar to air traffic control for aircraft.\n\n\n6A102\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Radiation hardened 'detectors', other than those specified in 6A002, specially designed or modified for protecting against nuclear effects (e.g. electromagnetic pulse (EMP), X-rays, combined blast and thermal effects) and usable for \"missiles\", designed or rated to withstand radiation levels which meet or exceed a total irradiation dose of 5 \u00d7 105 rads (silicon).\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nIn 6A102, a 'detector' is defined as a mechanical, electrical, optical or chemical device that automatically identifies and records, or registers a stimulus such as an environmental change in pressure or temperature, an electrical or electromagnetic signal or radiation from a radioactive material. For radar, see Category 6.\n\n\n7A001\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Accelerometers as follows and specially designed components therefor:\n\n\nN.B.:SEE ALSO 7A101.\n\n\nN.B.:For angular or rotational accelerometers, see 7A001.b.\n\n\na.Linear accelerometers having any of the following:\n\n\n1.Specified to function at linear acceleration levels less than or equal to 15 g and having any of the following:\n\n\na.A \"bias\" \"stability\" of less (better) than 130 micro g with respect to a fixed calibration value over a period of one year; or\n\n\nb.A \"scale factor\" \"stability\" of less (better) than 130 ppm with respect to a fixed calibration value over a period of one year;\n\n\n2.Specified to function at linear acceleration levels exceeding 15 g but less than or equal to 100 g and having all of the following:\n\n\n\n\na.A \"bias\" \"repeatability\" of less (better) than 1250 micro g over a period of one year; and\n\n\nb.A \"scale factor\" \"repeatability\" of less (better) than 1250 ppm over a period of one year; or\n\n\n3.Designed for use in inertial navigation or guidance systems and specified to function at linear acceleration levels exceeding 100 g;\n\n\nNote:7A001.a.1. and 7A001.a.2. do not control accelerometers limited to measurement of only vibration or shock.\n\n\nb.Angular or rotational accelerometers, specified to function at linear acceleration levels exceeding 100 g.\n\n\n7A002\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Gyros or angular rate sensors, having any of the following and specially designed components therefor:\n\n\nN.B.:SEE ALSO 7A102.\n\n\nN.B.:For angular or rotational accelerometers, see 7A001.b.\n\n\na.Specified to function at linear acceleration levels less than or equal to 100 g and having any of the following:\n\n\n1.A rate range of less than 500 degrees per second and having any of the following:\n\n\na.A \"bias\" \"stability\" of less (better) than 0,5 degree per hour, when measured in a 1 g environment over a period of one month, and with respect to a fixed calibration value; or\n\n\nb.An \"angle random walk\" of less (better) than or equal to 0.0035 degree per square root hour; or\n\n\nNote:7A002.a.1.b. does not control \"spinning mass gyros\".\n\n\n2.A rate range greater than or equal to 500 degrees per second and having any of the following:\n\n\na.A \"bias\" \"stability\" of less (better) than 4 degrees per hour, when measured in a 1 g environment over a period of three minutes, and with respect to a fixed calibration value; or\n\n\nb.An \"angle random walk\" of less (better) than or equal to 0,1 degree per square root hour; or\n\n\nNote:7A002.a.2.b. does not control \"spinning mass gyros\".\n\n\nb.Specified to function at linear acceleration levels exceeding 100 g.\n\n\n7A003\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0'Inertial measurement equipment or systems', having any of the following:\n\n\nN.B.:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0SEE ALSO 7A103.\n\n\n\n\nNote 1:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0'Inertial measurement equipment or systems' incorporate accelerometers or gyroscopes to measure changes in velocity and orientation in order to determine or maintain heading or position without requiring an external reference once aligned. 'Inertial measurement equipment or systems' include:\n\n\n\u2013Attitude and Heading Reference Systems (AHRSs);\n\n\n\u2013Gyrocompasses;\n\n\n\u2013Inertial Measurement Units (IMUs);\n\n\n\u2013Inertial Navigation Systems (INSs);\n\n\n\u2013Inertial Reference Systems (IRSs);\n\n\n\u2013Inertial Reference Units (IRUs).\n\n\nNote 2:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a07A003 does not control 'inertial measurement equipment or systems' which are certified for use on \"civil aircraft\" by civil aviation authorities of one or more EU Member States or Wassenaar Arrangement Participating States.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.'Positional aiding references' independently provide position, and include:\n\n\na.Global Navigation Satellite Systems (GNSS);\n\n\nb.\"Data-Based Referenced Navigation\" (\"DBRN\").\n\n\n2.'Circular Error Probable' ('CEP') - In a circular normal distribution, the radius of the circle containing 50 % of the individual measurements being made, or the radius of the circle within which there is a 50 % probability of being located.\n\n\na.Designed for \"aircraft\", land vehicles or vessels, providing position without the use of 'positional aiding references', and having any of the following accuracies subsequent to normal alignment:\n\n\n1.0,8 nautical miles per hour (nm/hr) 'Circular Error Probable' ('CEP') rate or less (better);\n\n\n2.0,5 % distanced travelled 'CEP' or less (better); or\n\n\n3.Total drift of 1 nautical mile 'CEP' or less (better) in a 24 hr period;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nThe performance parameters in 7A003.a.1., 7A003.a.2. and 7A003.a.3. typically apply to 'inertial measurement equipment or systems' designed for \"aircraft\", vehicles and vessels, respectively. These parameters result from the utilisation of specialised non-positional aiding references (e.g., altimeter, odometer, velocity log). As a consequence, the specified performance values cannot be readily converted between these parameters. Equipment designed for multiple platforms are evaluated against each applicable entry 7A003.a.1., 7A003.a.2., or 7A003.a.3.\n\n\nb.Designed for \"aircraft\", land vehicles or vessels, with an embedded 'positional aiding reference' and providing position after loss of all 'positional aiding references' for a period of up to 4 minutes, having an accuracy of less (better) than 10 meters 'CEP';\n\n\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n7A003.b. refers to systems in which 'inertial measurement equipment or systems' and other independent 'positional aiding references' are built into a single unit (i.e., embedded) in order to achieve improved performance.\n\n\nc.Designed for \"aircraft\", land vehicles or vessels, providing heading or True North determination and having any of the following:\n\n\n1.A maximum operating angular rate less (lower) than 500 deg/s and a heading accuracy without the use of 'positional aiding references' equal to or less (better) than 0,07 deg sec(Lat) (equivalent to 6 arc minutes rms at 45 degrees latitude); or\n\n\n2.A maximum operating angular rate equal to or greater (higher) than 500 deg/s and a heading accuracy without the use of 'positional aiding references' equal to or less (better) than 0,2 deg sec(Lat) (equivalent to 17 arc minutes rms at 45 degrees latitude); or\n\n\nd.Providing acceleration measurements or angular rate measurements, in more than one dimension, and having any of the following:\n\n\n1.Performance specified by 7A001 or 7A002 along any axis, without the use of any aiding references; or\n\n\n2.Being \"space-qualified\" and providing angular rate measurements having an \"angle random walk\" along any axis of less (better) than or equal to 0,1 degree per square root hour.\n\n\nNote:7A003.d.2. does not control 'inertial measurement equipment or systems' that contain \"spinning mass gyros\" as the only type of gyro.\n\n\n7A004\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0'Star trackers' and components therefor, as follows:\n\n\nN.B.:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0SEE ALSO 7A104.\n\n\na.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0'Star trackers' with a specified azimuth accuracy of equal to or less (better) than 20 seconds of arc throughout the specified lifetime of the equipment;\n\n\nb.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Components specially designed for equipment specified in 7A004.a. as follows:\n\n\n1.Optical heads or baffles;\n\n\n2.Data processing units.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Star trackers' are also referred to as stellar attitude sensors or gyro-astro compasses.\n\n\n7A005\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Global Navigation Satellite Systems (GNSS) receiving equipment having any of the following and specially designed components therefor:\n\n\nN.B.:SEE ALSO 7A105.\n\n\nN.B.:For equipment specially designed for military use, see Military Goods Controls.\n\n\n\n\na.Employing a decryption algorithm specially designed or modified for government use to access the ranging code for position and time; or\n\n\nb.Employing 'adaptive antenna systems'.\n\n\nNote:7A005.b. does not control GNSS receiving equipment that only uses components designed to filter, switch, or combine signals from multiple omni-directional antennae that do not implement adaptive antenna techniques.\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nFor the purposes of 7A005.b 'adaptive antenna systems' dynamically generate one or more spatial nulls in an antenna array pattern by signal processing in the time domain or frequency domain.\n\n\n7A006\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Airborne altimeters operating at frequencies other than 4.2 to 4.4 GHz inclusive and having any of the following:\n\n\nN.B.:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0SEE ALSO 7A106.\n\n\na.\"Power management\"; or\n\n\nb.Using phase shift key modulation.\n\n\n7A008\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Underwater sonar navigation systems using doppler velocity or correlation velocity logs integrated with a heading source and having a positioning accuracy of equal to or less (better) than 3 % of distance travelled 'Circular Error Probable' ('CEP') and specially designed components therefor.\n\n\nNote:7A008 does not control systems specially designed for installation on surface vessels or systems requiring acoustic beacons or buoys to provide positioning data.\n\n\nN.B.:See 6A001.a. for acoustic systems, and 6A001.b. for correlation-velocity and Doppler-velocity sonar log equipment.\n\n\nSee 8A002 for other marine systems.\n\n\n7A101\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Linear accelerometers, other than those specified in 7A001, designed for use in inertial navigation systems or in guidance systems of all types, usable in 'missiles', having all the following characteristics, and specially designed components therefor:\n\n\na.A \"bias\" \"repeatability\" of less (better) than 1250 micro g; and\n\n\nb.A \"scale factor\" \"repeatability\" of less (better) than 1250 ppm;\n\n\nNote:7A101 does not control accelerometers specially designed and developed as Measurement While Drilling (MWD) Sensors for use in downhole well service operations.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.In 7A101 'missile' means complete rocket systems and unmanned aerial vehicle systems capable of a range exceeding 300 km;\n\n\n2.In 7A101 the measurement of \"bias\" and \"scale factor\" refers to a one sigma standard deviation with respect to a fixed calibration over a period of one year;\n\n\n\n\n7A102\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0All types of gyros, other than those specified in 7A002, usable in 'missiles', with a rated \"drift rate\" 'stability' of less than 0.5 \u00b0 (1 sigma or rms) per hour in a 1 g environment and specially designed components therefor.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.In 7A102 'missile' means complete rocket systems and unmanned aerial vehicle systems capable of a range exceeding 300 km.\n\n\n2.In 7A102 'stability' is defined as a measure of the ability of a specific mechanism or performance coefficient to remain invariant when continuously exposed to a fixed operating condition (IEEE STD 528-2001 paragraph 2,247).\n\n\n7A103\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Instrumentation, navigation equipment and systems, other than those specified in 7A003, as follows; and specially designed components therefor:\n\n\na.Inertial or other equipment, using accelerometers or gyros as follows, and systems incorporating such equipment:\n\n\n1.Accelerometers specified in 7A001.a.3., 7A001.b. or 7A101 or gyros specified in 7A002 or 7A102; or\n\n\n2.Accelerometers specified in 7A001,a,1, or 7A001,a,2, designed for use in inertial navigation systems or in guidance systems of all types, and usable in 'missiles';\n\n\nNote:7A103.a. does not specify equipment containing accelerometers specified in 7A001 where such accelerometers are specially designed and developed as MWD (Measurement While Drilling) sensors for use in down-hole well services operations.\n\n\nb.Integrated flight instrument systems which include gyrostabilisers or automatic pilots, designed or modified for use in 'missiles';\n\n\nc.'Integrated navigation systems', designed or modified for 'missiles' and capable of providing a navigational accuracy of 200 m Circle of Equal Probability (CEP) or less;\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nAn 'integrated navigation system' typically incorporates the following components:\n\n\n1.An inertial measurement device (e.g., an attitude and heading reference system, inertial reference unit, or inertial navigation system);\n\n\n2.One or more external sensors used to update the position and/or velocity, either periodically or continuously throughout the flight (e.g., satellite navigation receiver, radar altimeter, and/or Doppler radar); and\n\n\n3.Integration hardware and software;\n\n\nd.Three axis magnetic heading sensors, designed or modified to be integrated with flight control and navigation systems, other than those specified in 6A006, having all the following characteristics, and specially designed components therefor;\n\n\n1.Internal tilt compensation in pitch (\u00b1 90 degrees) and roll (\u00b1 180 degrees) axes;\n\n\n2.Capable of providing azimuthal accuracy better (less) than 0,5 degrees rms at latitude of \u00b1 80 degrees, reference to local magnetic field.\n\n\nNote:Flight control and navigation systems in 7A103.d. include gyrostabilizers, automatic pilots and inertial navigation systems.\n\n\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nIn 7A103 'missile' means complete rocket systems and unmanned aerial vehicle systems capable of a range exceeding 300 km.\n\n\n7A104\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Gyro-astro compasses and other devices, other than those specified in 7A004, which derive position or orientation by means of automatically tracking celestial bodies or satellites and specially designed components therefor.\n\n\n7A105\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Receiving equipment for Global Navigation Satellite Systems (GNSS; By following the manufacturer's manual, the cause of the failure may be localised at the level of the malfunctioning Line Replaceable Unit (LRU). The operator then removes the LRU and replaces it with a spare.\n\n\n2.'Maintenance Level II'\n\n\nThe defective LRU is sent to the maintenance workshop (the manufacturer's or that of the operator responsible for level II maintenance). At the maintenance workshop, the malfunctioning LRU is tested by various appropriate means to verify and localise the defective Shop Replaceable Assembly (SRA) module responsible for the failure. This SRA is removed and replaced by an operative spare. The defective SRA (or possibly the complete LRU) is then shipped to the manufacturer. 'Maintenance Level II' does not include the disassembly or repair of controlled accelerometers or gyro sensors.\n\n\n7B002\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Equipment specially designed to characterize mirrors for ring \"laser\" gyros, as follows:\n\n\nN.B.:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0SEE ALSO 7B102.\n\n\na.Scatterometers having a measurement accuracy of 10 ppm or less (better);\n\n\nb.Profilometers having a measurement accuracy of 0,5 nm (5 angstrom) or less (better).\n\n\n7B003\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Equipment specially designed for the \"production\" of equipment specified in and fill stations;\n\n\n\u2013Centrifuge fixtures for gyro bearings;\n\n\n\n\n\u2013Accelerometer axis align stations;\n\n\n\u2013Fibre optic gyro coil winding machines.\n\n\n7B102\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Reflectometers specially designed to characterise mirrors, for \"laser\" gyros, having a measurement accuracy of 50 ppm or less (better).\n\n\n7B103\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Production facilities\" and \"production equipment\" as follows:\n\n\na.\"Production facilities\" specially designed for equipment specified in of \"active flight control systems\" that automate airframe stability controls.\n\n\nb.Having any of the following:\n\n\n1.Corrects an aerodynamically unstable airframe, measured at any point in the design flight envelope, that would lose recoverable control if not corrected within 0.5 seconds;\n\n\n2.Couples controls in two or more axes while compensating for 'abnormal changes in aircraft state';\n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\n'Abnormal changes in aircraft state' include in-flight structural damage, loss of engine thrust, disabled control surface, or destabilizing shifts in cargo load.\n\n\n3.Performs the functions specified in 7E004.b.5.; or\n\n\nNote:7E004.b.7.b.3. does not control autopilots.\n\n\n\n\n4.Enables aircraft to have stable controlled flight, other than during take-off or landing, at greater than 18 degrees angle of attack, 15 degrees side slip, 15 degrees/second pitch or yaw rate, or 90 degrees/second roll rate;\n\n\n8.\"Technology\" \"required\" for deriving the functional requirements for \"fly-by-wire systems\" to achieve all of the following:\n\n\na.No loss of control of the aircraft in the event of a consecutive sequence of any two individual faults within the \"fly-by-wire system\"; and\n\n\nb.Probability of loss of control of the aircraft being less (better) than 1x10-9 failures per flight hour;\n\n\nNote:7E004.b. does not control technology associated with common computer elements and utilities (e.g., input signal acquisition, output signal transmission, computer program and data loading, built-in test, task scheduling mechanisms) not providing a specific flight control system function.\n\n\nc.\"Technology\" for the \"development\" of helicopter systems, as follows:\n\n\n1.Multi-axis fly-by-wire or fly-by-light controllers, which combine the functions of at least two of the following into one controlling element:\n\n\na.Collective controls;\n\n\nb.Cyclic controls;\n\n\nc.Yaw controls;\n\n\n2.\"Circulation-controlled anti-torque or circulation-controlled directional control systems\";\n\n\n3.Rotor blades incorporating \"variable geometry airfoils\", for use in systems using individual blade control.\n\n\n7E101\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Technology\" according to the General Technology Note for the \"use\" of equipment specified in 7A001 to 7A006, 7A101 to 7A106, 7A115 to 7A117, 7B001, 7B002, 7B003, 7B102, 7B103, 7D101 to 7D103.\n\n\n7E102\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Technology\" for protection of avionics and electrical subsystems against electromagnetic pulse (EMP) and electromagnetic interference (EMI) hazards, from external sources, as follows:\n\n\na.Design \"technology\" for shielding systems;\n\n\nb.Design \"technology\" for the configuration of hardened designed components therefor.\n\n\nN.B.:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0SEE ALSO 9A111 AND 9A118.\n\n\n9A012\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\"Unmanned aerial vehicles\" (\"UAVs\"), unmanned \"airships\", related, equipment and components, as follows:\n\n\nN.B.:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0SEE ALSO 9A112.\n\n\na.\"UAVs\" or unmanned \"airships\", designed to have controlled flight out of the direct 'natural vision' of the 'operator' and having any of the following:\n\n\n1.Having all of the following:\n\n\na.A maximum 'endurance' greater than or equal to 30 minutes but less than 1 hour; and\n\n\nb.Designed to take-off and have stable controlled flight in wind gusts equal to or exceeding 46,3 km/h (25 knots); or\n\n\n2.A maximum 'endurance' of 1 hour or greater;\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n\n\n1.For the purposes of 9A012.a., 'operator' is a person who initiates or commands the \"UAV\" or unmanned \"airship\" flight.\n\n\n2.For the purposes of 9A012.a., 'endurance' is to be calculated for ISA conditions (ISO 2533:1975) at sea level in zero wind.\n\n\n3.For the purposes of 9A012.a., 'natural vision' means unaided human sight, with or without corrective lenses.\n\n\nb.Related equipment and components, as follows:\n\n\n1.Not used\n\n\n2.Not used\n\n\n3.Equipment or components, specially designed to convert a manned \"aircraft\" or manned \"airship\", to a \"UAV\" or unmanned \"airship\", specified in 9A012.a.;\n\n\n4.Air breathing reciprocating or rotary internal combustion type engines, specially designed or modified to propel \"UAVs\" or unmanned \"airships\", at altitudes above 15240 metres (50,000 feet).\n\n\n9A101\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Turbojet and turbofan engines, other than those specified in 9A001, as follows;\n\n\na.Engines having both of the following characteristics:\n\n\n1.'Maximum thrust value' greater than 400 N (achieved un-installed) excluding civil certified engines with a 'maximum thrust value' greater than 8890 N (achieved un-installed), and\n\n\n2.Specific fuel consumption of 0,15 kg/N/hr or less (at maximum continuous power at sea level static conditions using the ICAO standard atmosphere); \n\n\nTechnical Note:\n\n\nFor the purpose of 9A101.a.1. 'maximum thrust value' is the manufacturers demonstrated maximum thrust for the engine type un-installed. The civil type certified thrust value will be equal or less than the manufacturers demonstrated maximum thrust for the engine type.\n\n\nb.Engines designed or modified for use in \"missiles\" or unmanned aerial vehicles specified in 9A012 or 9A112.a,\n\n\n9A102\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0'Turboprop engine systems' specially designed for unmanned aerial vehicles specified in 9A012 or 9A112.a, and specially designed components therefor, having a 'maximum power' greater than 10 kW.\n\n\nNote:\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a09A102 does not control civil certified engines.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.For the purposes of 9A102 a 'turboprop engine system' incorporates all of the following:\n\n\na.Turboshaft engine; and\n\n\n\n\nb.Power transmission system to transfer the power to a propeller.\n\n\n2.For the purposes of 9A102 the 'maximum power' is achieved uninstalled at sea level static conditions using ICAO standard atmosphere.\n\n\n9A104\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Sounding rockets, capable of a range of at probes); or\n\n\n5.Thrust tabs.\n\n\nd.Liquid, slurry and gel propellant (including oxidisers) control systems, and specially designed components therefor, usable in \"missiles\", designed or modified to operate in vibration environments greater than 10 g rms between 20 Hz and 2 kHz.\n\n\n\n\nNote:The only servo valves, pumps and gas turbines specified in 9A106.d., are the following:\n\n\na.Servo ms;\n\n\nb.Pumps, for liquid propellants, with shaft speeds equal to or greater than 8000 r.p.m. at a maximum operating mode or with discharge pressures equal to or greater than 7 MPa.\n\n\nc.Gas turbines, for liquid propellant turbopumps, with shaft speeds equal to or greater than 8000 r.p.m. at the maximum operating mode.\n\n\ne.Combustion chambers and nozzles, usable in \"missiles\", space follows:\n\n\na.\"Unmanned aerial vehicles\" (\"UAVs\") capable of a range of 300 km;\n\n\nb.\"Unmanned aerial vehicles\" (\"UAVs\") having all of the following:\n\n\n1.Having any of the following:\n\n\na.An autonomous flight control and navigation capability; or\n\n\nb.Capability of controlled flight out of the direct vision range involving a human operator; and\n\n\n2.Having any of the following:\n\n\na.Incorporating an aerosol dispensing system/mechanism with a capacity greater than 20 litres; or\n\n\nb.Designed or modified to incorporate an aerosol dispensing system/mechanism with a capacity greater than 20 litres.\n\n\nTechnical Notes:\n\n\n1.An aerosol consists of particulate or liquids other than fuel components, by products or additives, as part of the \"payload\" to be dispersed in the atmosphere. Examples of aerosols include pesticides for crop dusting and dry chemicals for cloud seeding.\n\n\n2.An aerosol dispensing system/mechanism contains all those devices (mechanical, electrical, hydraulic, etc.), which are necessary for storage and dispersion of an aerosol into the atmosphere. This includes the possibility of aerosol injection into the combustion exhaust vapour and into the propeller slip stream.\n\n\n\n\n9A115\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Launch support equipment as using either of the following:\n\n\na.Doppler laser method;\n\n\nb.Forward laser diffraction method.\n\n\n2.In 9A350 'VMD' means Volume Median Diameter and for water-based systems this equates to Mass Median Diameter (MMD).\n\n\n9BTest, Inspection and Production Equipment\n\n\n9B001\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Equipment, tooling or fixtures, specially designed for manufacturing gas turbine blades, vanes or 'bare table' means a flat table, or surface, with no fixture or fittings.\n\n\nb.Environmental chambers capable of simulating the following flight conditions:\n\n\n1.Acoustic environments at an controlled when used for repair or overhaul.
